=== Iteration 1 - [2026-05-01 07:45:42] ===
PLAN:
  === ADJUSTED ENVIRONMENT SETUP PLAN (for CPU-only Linux x86_64 system) ===
  ---
  **Summary:**  
  Your hardware environment is Linux x86_64 without an NVIDIA GPU. Consequently, CUDA, GPU drivers, and GPU-accelerated PyTorch builds are not applicable. The plan below is adjusted to fully support CPU-only operation, leveraging CPU training/offload modes, and ensuring compatibility with your hardware. Storage and memory requirements remain important and unchanged. This plan assumes no GPU acceleration and instructs necessary changes accordingly.
  ---
  1. DOWNLOADS NEEDED (ADJUSTED FOR CPU-ONLY):
  - Git (latest stable version) for cloning the repository  
  - Conda (Anaconda or Miniconda) with Python 3.10 environment support  
  - **No NVIDIA GPU driver or CUDA Toolkit installation required** (remove all CUDA 12.4 and related dependencies)  
  - PyTorch 2.6.0 **CPU-only version** (install CPU-only PyTorch build)  
  - Additional Python packages: torchvision 0.21.0, torchaudio 2.6.0 (CPU-only builds if applicable)  
  - Python packages (via pip): tqdm, plyfile, psutil, numba, opencv-python, scipy, matplotlib, pandas, imageio, imageio-ffmpeg, requests, tabulate  
  - Build tools for compiling submodules (e.g., gcc/g++, setuptools) compatible with your Linux OS and x86_64 architecture  
  - Optional: Black code formatter (pip install black)  
  - Adequate local disk storage:  
    - Minimum ~500GB free disk space recommended for MatrixCity BigCity dataset decoded images (as before)  
    - At least 50GB free disk for models/outputs  
    - Fast local disk strongly recommended especially for large datasets (avoid network filesystems)  
  - System memory:  
    - Minimum 32GB RAM recommended for regular experiments  
    - For large-scale datasets (BigCity 102M), 100GB+ CPU RAM recommended for pinned memory allocations  
    - Mip360 and Rubble 4K datasets’ CPU RAM requirements remain unchanged  
  - Optional: bash shell for running example scripts  
  - Notes on offload strategies:  
    - `--clm_offload` **can still be used** in CPU-only mode but CUDA kernels in `clm_kernels` are CUDA-based and require GPU presence; thus, **`--clm_offload` cannot be used on CPU-only systems** because it depends on CUDA and GPU drivers  
    - `--naive_offload` uses CPU pinned memory but also depends on CUDA GPU for data transfer and training; thus, **`--naive_offload` is not applicable without GPU**  
    - **Only `--no_offload` training strategy is feasible and supported on your CPU-only system** (full training on CPU without GPU offloading)  
    - `--no_offload` uses `gsplat` rendering kernels which are native CPU-compatible (compiled submodules support CPU)  
  - Version compatibility requirements:  
    - Python 3.10  
    - PyTorch 2.6.0 CPU-only build  
    - Compatible build tools (gcc/g++, make, python-dev headers) for compiling submodules  
  - Environment variables related to CUDA allocator config (`PYTORCH_CUDA_ALLOC_CONF`) are **not applicable** and should be omitted  
  ---
  2. FILES TO CREATE (UNCHANGED):
  - `.condarc` (optional) for conda configuration  
  - `environment.yml` (optional) with Python 3.10 and all pip packages (adjust PyTorch and torchvision to CPU-only versions)  
  - `README.md`, `LICENSE.txt` as before  
  - Shell scripts for automation (same as before)  
  - Dataset experiment scripts (`release_scripts/bigcity.sh`, `mip360.sh`, `rubble4k.sh`) can be used with `--no_offload` only  
  - Documentation files remain the same  
  - Ensure inclusion and compilation of CPU-compatible submodules (`gsplat`, `clm_kernels` submodule compilation may fail or be skipped due to lack of CUDA; skip or disable `clm_kernels` build)  
  - Ensure `gaussian_model.py` and `engine.py` support `GaussianModelNoOffload` and no GPU dependencies  
  - Omit environment variable config for CUDA allocator  
  - Notes on large disk/memory requirements for datasets remain unchanged  
  ---
  3. NECESSARY TEST CASES (ADJUSTED FOR CPU-ONLY):
  - Verify successful cloning with submodules (note: `clm_kernels` submodule may fail to build or be skipped)  
  - Test Python environment activation and package imports including CPU-only torch, torchvision, torchaudio, numba, opencv, etc.  
  - **Test that torch.cuda.is_available() returns False** and no CUDA version check is needed  
  - Test compilation and import of CPU-compatible submodules only (`gsplat`, `cpu-adam`, `fast-tsp`, `simple-knn`)  
  - Run small sanity training run using the `--no_offload` strategy on a small dataset (e.g., Mip360) with batch size 4 or smaller to verify pipeline correctness and environment setup  
  - Confirm microbatch pipelining and gradient accumulation run without errors on CPU  
  - Validate dataset loading and decoding mechanism as before  
  - **Skip all tests related to `--clm_offload` and `--naive_offload` strategies** (these require GPU and CUDA)  
  - Confirm training results and logs for `--no_offload` only  
  - Validate dataset decoding reuse and caching as before  
  - Validate results aggregation from logs for `--no_offload` runs  
  - Confirm no CUDA-related errors during training or submodule imports

  4. COMPLETE TODO LIST (ADJUSTED):
  **Step 1: Prepare Hardware and System**  
  - Confirm no NVIDIA GPU present; CUDA and GPU driver installation omitted  
  - Ensure system has minimum 32GB CPU RAM (≥100GB recommended for large BigCity experiments)  
  - Ensure adequate disk space as specified  
  - Install standard Linux build tools: gcc, g++, make, python3-dev headers  
  Verification:

  **Step 2: Install Conda and Create Python Environment**  
  - Install Miniconda or Anaconda (latest stable version for Linux x86_64)  
  - Create conda environment with Python 3.10:  
    ```shell  
    conda create -n clm_gs_cpu python=3.10 -y  
    conda activate clm_gs_cpu  
    ```  
  - Install CPU-only PyTorch 2.6.0 and related CPU-only torchvision and torchaudio packages:  
    ```shell  
    pip install torch==2.6.0+cpu torchvision==0.21.0+cpu torchaudio==2.6.0 --extra-index-url https://download.pytorch.org/whl/cpu  
    ```  
  - Install other pip dependencies:  
    ```shell  
    pip install tqdm plyfile psutil numba opencv-python scipy matplotlib pandas imageio imageio-ffmpeg requests tabulate  
    ```  
  Verification:  
  - Run `python -c "import torch; print(torch.__version__)"` and confirm CPU-only build (no CUDA)  
  - Run `python -c "import torch; print(torch.cuda.is_available())"` which should print `False`  
  ---
  **Step 3: Clone Repository with Submodules**  
  - Clone with recursive submodules as before:

    ```shell  
    git clone git@github.com:nyu-systems/CLM-GS.git --recursive  
    cd CLM-GS  
    ```  
  - If needed:  
    ```shell  
    git submodule update --init --recursive  
    ```  
  Verification:  
  - Confirm all submodules cloned  
  - Note: `clm_kernels` submodule may not build without CUDA (skip build step for this submodule)

  ---
  **Step 12: Troubleshooting and Error Handling**  
  - If submodule compilation fails for `clm_kernels`, skip or disable it (not needed for CPU-only training)  
  - If PyTorch CUDA-dependent imports or calls occur, ensure code paths for `--clm_offload` and `--naive_offload` are not executed  
  - Monitor CPU memory usage to prevent OOM; adjust batch size and prealloc_capacity accordingly  
  - If training is very slow on CPU, consider smaller dataset scales or hardware upgrades  
  - For dataset loading errors, confirm correct local path and dataset format  
  - Confirm no attempts to use GPU features during training or script runs  
  ---
  **Summary of Key Adjustments:**
  | Aspect                          | Original Plan (GPU)                                | Adjusted Plan (CPU-only)                          |
  |--------------------------------|--------------------------------------------------|--------------------------------------------------|
  | GPU Driver & CUDA Toolkit       | Install CUDA 12.4 & GPU driver                    | **Omit CUDA & GPU driver installation**           |
  | PyTorch Version                | PyTorch 2.6.0 with CUDA 12.4 support              | PyTorch 2.6.0 CPU-only build                       |
  | Offload Strategies             | Support `--clm_offload`, `--naive_offload`, `--no_offload` | **Only support `--no_offload`; skip others**      |
  | Environment Variables          | Set `PYTORCH_CUDA_ALLOC_CONF`                      | **Do not set CUDA-related env vars**               |
  | Submodules                     | Compile all including `clm_kernels` (CUDA kernels) | Skip or disable `clm_kernels` compilation          |
  | Training Scripts               | Run all offload modes                              | Run only with `--no_offload`                        |
  | Hardware Requirements          | GPU with ≥24GB VRAM for large-scale, 32GB+ CPU RAM | No GPU needed; maintain CPU RAM and disk requirements |
  | Dataset Decoding & Storage     | Fast local disk; same requirements                 | Same requirements                                  |
  | Testing                       | Include CUDA availability and GPU-specific tests  | Skip CUDA/GPU tests; test CPU-only training        |
  ---
  This adjusted plan ensures your environment setup and workflow are compatible with your CPU-only Linux x86_64 hardware, avoiding GPU dependencies, while preserving dataset handling, model training (with `--no_offload`), and experiment reproducibility.

DOCKERFILE:
  FROM ubuntu:22.04
  ENV DEBIAN_FRONTEND=noninteractive
  ENV LANG=C.UTF-8 LC_ALL=C.UTF-8
  # Install system dependencies
  RUN apt-get update && apt-get install -y --no-install-recommends \
      git \
      curl \
      wget \
      ca-certificates \
      build-essential \
      gcc \
      g++ \
      make \
      python3.10 \
      python3.10-dev \
      python3-pip \
      python3-setuptools \
      python3-venv \
      libgl1-mesa-glx \
      libglib2.0-0 \
      bash \
      && rm -rf /var/lib/apt/lists/*
  # Symlink python3.10 to python and pip3 to pip
  RUN update-alternatives --install /usr/bin/python python /usr/bin/python3.10 1 && \
      python -m pip install --upgrade pip setuptools wheel
  # Install Miniconda (latest for Linux x86_64)
  ENV CONDA_DIR=/opt/conda
  RUN wget --quiet https://repo.anaconda.com/miniconda/Miniconda3-latest-Linux-x86_64.sh -O /tmp/miniconda.sh && \
      bash /tmp/miniconda.sh -b -p $CONDA_DIR && \
      rm /tmp/miniconda.sh
  ENV PATH=$CONDA_DIR/bin:$PATH
  # Create conda environment with python 3.10
  RUN conda create -n clm_gs_cpu python=3.10 -y && \
      conda clean -afy
  SHELL ["conda", "run", "-n", "clm_gs_cpu", "/bin/bash", "-c"]
  # Activate environment and install CPU-only PyTorch and dependencies
  RUN pip install --upgrade pip setuptools wheel && \
      pip install \
        torch==2.6.0+cpu \
        torchvision==0.21.0+cpu \
        torchaudio==2.6.0 \
        --extra-index-url https://download.pytorch.org/whl/cpu && \
      pip install \
        tqdm \
        plyfile \
        psutil \
        numba \
        opencv-python \
        scipy \
        matplotlib \
        pandas \
        imageio \
        imageio-ffmpeg \
        requests \
        tabulate \
        black
  WORKDIR /root
  # Clone the main repository with submodules
  RUN git clone --recursive https://github.com/nyu-systems/CLM-GS.git /root/CLM-GS
  WORKDIR /root/CLM-GS
  # Update submodules recursively (in case)
  RUN git submodule update --init --recursive
  # Install CPU-compatible submodules only, skipping clm_kernels (due to CUDA dependency)
  # The clm_kernels directory remains but is not installed
  RUN pip install --no-build-isolation ./submodules/cpu-adam && \
      pip install ./submodules/fast-tsp && \
      pip install --no-build-isolation ./submodules/gsplat && \
      pip install --no-build-isolation ./submodules/simple-knn
  # Set default shell to bash and start at repo root
  CMD ["/bin/bash"]

PLAN:
  === ADJUSTED ENVIRONMENT SETUP PLAN (for CPU-only Linux x86_64 system) ===
  ---
  **Summary:**  
  Your hardware environment is Linux x86_64 without an NVIDIA GPU. Consequently, CUDA, GPU drivers, and GPU-accelerated PyTorch builds are not applicable. The plan below is adjusted to fully support CPU-only operation, leveraging CPU training/offload modes, and ensuring compatibility with your hardware. Storage and memory requirements remain important and unchanged. This plan assumes no GPU acceleration and instructs necessary changes accordingly.
  ---
  1. DOWNLOADS NEEDED (ADJUSTED FOR CPU-ONLY):
  - Git (latest stable version) for cloning the repository  
  - Conda (Anaconda or Miniconda) with Python 3.10 environment support  
  - **No NVIDIA GPU driver or CUDA Toolkit installation required** (remove all CUDA 12.4 and related dependencies)  
  - PyTorch 2.6.0 **CPU-only version** (install CPU-only PyTorch build)  
  - Additional Python packages: torchvision 0.21.0, torchaudio 2.6.0 (CPU-only builds if applicable)  
  - Python packages (via pip): tqdm, plyfile, psutil, numba, opencv-python, scipy, matplotlib, pandas, imageio, imageio-ffmpeg, requests, tabulate  
  - Build tools for compiling submodules (e.g., gcc/g++, setuptools) compatible with your Linux OS and x86_64 architecture  
  - Optional: Black code formatter (pip install black)  
  - Adequate local disk storage:  
    - Minimum ~500GB free disk space recommended for MatrixCity BigCity dataset decoded images (as before)  
    - At least 50GB free disk for models/outputs  
    - Fast local disk strongly recommended especially for large datasets (avoid network filesystems)  
  - System memory:  
    - Minimum 32GB RAM recommended for regular experiments  
    - For large-scale datasets (BigCity 102M), 100GB+ CPU RAM recommended for pinned memory allocations  
    - Mip360 and Rubble 4K datasets’ CPU RAM requirements remain unchanged  
  - Optional: bash shell for running example scripts  
  - Notes on offload strategies:  
    - `--clm_offload` **can still be used** in CPU-only mode but CUDA kernels in `clm_kernels` are CUDA-based and require GPU presence; thus, **`--clm_offload` cannot be used on CPU-only systems** because it depends on CUDA and GPU drivers  
    - `--naive_offload` uses CPU pinned memory but also depends on CUDA GPU for data transfer and training; thus, **`--naive_offload` is not applicable without GPU**  
    - **Only `--no_offload` training strategy is feasible and supported on your CPU-only system** (full training on CPU without GPU offloading)  
    - `--no_offload` uses `gsplat` rendering kernels which are native CPU-compatible (compiled submodules support CPU)  
  - Version compatibility requirements:  
    - Python 3.10  
    - PyTorch 2.6.0 CPU-only build  
    - Compatible build tools (gcc/g++, make, python-dev headers) for compiling submodules  
  - Environment variables related to CUDA allocator config (`PYTORCH_CUDA_ALLOC_CONF`) are **not applicable** and should be omitted  
  ---
  2. FILES TO CREATE (UNCHANGED):
  - `.condarc` (optional) for conda configuration  
  - `environment.yml` (optional) with Python 3.10 and all pip packages (adjust PyTorch and torchvision to CPU-only versions)  
  - `README.md`, `LICENSE.txt` as before  
  - Shell scripts for automation (same as before)  
  - Dataset experiment scripts (`release_scripts/bigcity.sh`, `mip360.sh`, `rubble4k.sh`) can be used with `--no_offload` only  
  - Documentation files remain the same  
  - Ensure inclusion and compilation of CPU-compatible submodules (`gsplat`, `clm_kernels` submodule compilation may fail or be skipped due to lack of CUDA; skip or disable `clm_kernels` build)  
  - Ensure `gaussian_model.py` and `engine.py` support `GaussianModelNoOffload` and no GPU dependencies  
  - Omit environment variable config for CUDA allocator  
  - Notes on large disk/memory requirements for datasets remain unchanged

  | Testing                       | Include CUDA availability and GPU-specific tests  | Skip CUDA/GPU tests; test CPU-only training        |

DOCKERFILE:
  FROM ubuntu:22.04
  ENV DEBIAN_FRONTEND=noninteractive
  ENV LANG=C.UTF-8 LC_ALL=C.UTF-8
  # Install system dependencies
  RUN apt-get update && apt-get install -y --no-install-recommends \
      git \
      curl \
      wget \
      ca-certificates \
      build-essential \
      gcc \
      g++ \
      make \
      python3.10 \
      python3.10-dev \
      python3-pip \
      python3-setuptools \
      python3-venv \
      libgl1-mesa-glx \
      libglib2.0-0 \
      bash \
      && rm -rf /var/lib/apt/lists/*
  # Symlink python3.10 to python and upgrade pip
  RUN update-alternatives --install /usr/bin/python python /usr/bin/python3.10 1 && \
      python -m pip install --upgrade pip setuptools wheel
  # Install Miniconda (latest for Linux x86_64)
  ENV CONDA_DIR=/opt/conda
  RUN wget --quiet https://repo.anaconda.com/miniconda/Miniconda3-latest-Linux-x86_64.sh -O /tmp/miniconda.sh && \
      bash /tmp/miniconda.sh -b -p $CONDA_DIR && \
      rm /tmp/miniconda.sh
  ENV PATH=$CONDA_DIR/bin:$PATH
  # Initialize conda and create environment with python 3.10, then install packages in one RUN
  RUN . $CONDA_DIR/etc/profile.d/conda.sh && \
      conda create -n clm_gs_cpu python=3.10 -y && \
      conda clean -afy && \
      conda activate clm_gs_cpu && \
      pip install --upgrade pip setuptools wheel && \
      pip install \
        torch==2.6.0+cpu \
        torchvision==0.21.0+cpu \
        torchaudio==2.6.0 \
        --extra-index-url https://download.pytorch.org/whl/cpu && \
      pip install \
        tqdm \
        plyfile \
        psutil \
        numba \
        opencv-python \
        scipy \
        matplotlib \
        pandas \
        imageio \
        imageio-ffmpeg \
        requests \
        tabulate \
        black
  WORKDIR /root
  # Clone the main repository with submodules
  RUN git clone --recursive https://github.com/nyu-systems/CLM-GS.git /root/CLM-GS
  WORKDIR /root/CLM-GS
  # Update submodules recursively (in case)
  RUN git submodule update --init --recursive
  # Install CPU-compatible submodules only, skipping clm_kernels (due to CUDA dependency)
  # Activate conda environment to install submodules
  RUN . $CONDA_DIR/etc/profile.d/conda.sh && conda activate clm_gs_cpu && \
      pip install --no-build-isolation ./submodules/cpu-adam && \
      pip install ./submodules/fast-tsp && \
      pip install --no-build-isolation ./submodules/gsplat && \
      pip install --no-build-isolation ./submodules/simple-knn
  # Set default shell to bash and start at repo root with conda environment activated
  CMD ["/bin/bash", "-c", ". /opt/conda/etc/profile.d/conda.sh && conda activate clm_gs_cpu && exec /bin/bash"]

=== Iteration 3 - [2026-05-01 07:46:28] ===
PLAN:
  === ADJUSTED ENVIRONMENT SETUP PLAN (for CPU-only Linux x86_64 system) ===
  ---
  **Summary:**  
  Your hardware environment is Linux x86_64 without an NVIDIA GPU. Consequently, CUDA, GPU drivers, and GPU-accelerated PyTorch builds are not applicable. The plan below is adjusted to fully support CPU-only operation, leveraging CPU training/offload modes, and ensuring compatibility with your hardware. Storage and memory requirements remain important and unchanged. This plan assumes no GPU acceleration and instructs necessary changes accordingly.
  ---
  1. DOWNLOADS NEEDED (ADJUSTED FOR CPU-ONLY):
  - Git (latest stable version) for cloning the repository  
  - Conda (Anaconda or Miniconda) with Python 3.10 environment support  
  - **No NVIDIA GPU driver or CUDA Toolkit installation required** (remove all CUDA 12.4 and related dependencies)  
  - PyTorch 2.6.0 **CPU-only version** (install CPU-only PyTorch build)  
  - Additional Python packages: torchvision 0.21.0, torchaudio 2.6.0 (CPU-only builds if applicable)  
  - Python packages (via pip): tqdm, plyfile, psutil, numba, opencv-python, scipy, matplotlib, pandas, imageio, imageio-ffmpeg, requests, tabulate  
  - Build tools for compiling submodules (e.g., gcc/g++, setuptools) compatible with your Linux OS and x86_64 architecture  
  - Optional: Black code formatter (pip install black)  
  - Adequate local disk storage:  
    - Minimum ~500GB free disk space recommended for MatrixCity BigCity dataset decoded images (as before)  
    - At least 50GB free disk for models/outputs  
    - Fast local disk strongly recommended especially for large datasets (avoid network filesystems)  
  - System memory:  
    - Minimum 32GB RAM recommended for regular experiments  
    - For large-scale datasets (BigCity 102M), 100GB+ CPU RAM recommended for pinned memory allocations  
    - Mip360 and Rubble 4K datasets’ CPU RAM requirements remain unchanged  
  - Optional: bash shell for running example scripts  
  - Notes on offload strategies:  
    - `--clm_offload` **can still be used** in CPU-only mode but CUDA kernels in `clm_kernels` are CUDA-based and require GPU presence; thus, **`--clm_offload` cannot be used on CPU-only systems** because it depends on CUDA and GPU drivers  
    - `--naive_offload` uses CPU pinned memory but also depends on CUDA GPU for data transfer and training; thus, **`--naive_offload` is not applicable without GPU**  
    - **Only `--no_offload` training strategy is feasible and supported on your CPU-only system** (full training on CPU without GPU offloading)  
    - `--no_offload` uses `gsplat` rendering kernels which are native CPU-compatible (compiled submodules support CPU)  
  - Version compatibility requirements:  
    - Python 3.10  
    - PyTorch 2.6.0 CPU-only build  
    - Compatible build tools (gcc/g++, make, python-dev headers) for compiling submodules  
  - Environment variables related to CUDA allocator config (`PYTORCH_CUDA_ALLOC_CONF`) are **not applicable** and should be omitted  
  ---
  2. FILES TO CREATE (UNCHANGED):
  - `.condarc` (optional) for conda configuration  
  - `environment.yml` (optional) with Python 3.10 and all pip packages (adjust PyTorch and torchvision to CPU-only versions)  
  - `README.md`, `LICENSE.txt` as before  
  - Shell scripts for automation (same as before)  
  - Dataset experiment scripts (`release_scripts/bigcity.sh`, `mip360.sh`, `rubble4k.sh`) can be used with `--no_offload` only  
  - Documentation files remain the same  
  - Ensure inclusion and compilation of CPU-compatible submodules (`gsplat`, `clm_kernels` submodule compilation may fail or be skipped due to lack of CUDA; skip or disable `clm_kernels` build)  
  - Ensure `gaussian_model.py` and `engine.py` support `GaussianModelNoOffload` and no GPU dependencies  
  - Omit environment variable config for CUDA allocator  
  - Notes on large disk/memory requirements for datasets remain unchanged  
  ---
  3. NECESSARY TEST CASES (ADJUSTED FOR CPU-ONLY):
  - Verify successful cloning with submodules (note: `clm_kernels` submodule may fail to build or be skipped)  
  - Test Python environment activation and package imports including CPU-only torch, torchvision, torchaudio, numba, opencv, etc.  
  - **Test that torch.cuda.is_available() returns False** and no CUDA version check is needed  
  - Test compilation and import of CPU-compatible submodules only (`gsplat`, `cpu-adam`, `fast-tsp`, `simple-knn`)  
  - Run small sanity training run using the `--no_offload` strategy on a small dataset (e.g., Mip360) with batch size 4 or smaller to verify pipeline correctness and environment setup  
  - Confirm microbatch pipelining and gradient accumulation run without errors on CPU  
  - Validate dataset loading and decoding mechanism as before  
  - **Skip all tests related to `--clm_offload` and `--naive_offload` strategies** (these require GPU and CUDA)  
  - Confirm training results and logs for `--no_offload` only  
  - Validate dataset decoding reuse and caching as before  
  - Validate results aggregation from logs for `--no_offload` runs  
  - Confirm no CUDA-related errors during training or submodule imports

  **Summary of Key Adjustments:**
  | Aspect                          | Original Plan (GPU)                                | Adjusted Plan (CPU-only)                          |
  |--------------------------------|--------------------------------------------------|--------------------------------------------------|
  | GPU Driver & CUDA Toolkit       | Install CUDA 12.4 & GPU driver                    | **Omit CUDA & GPU driver installation**           |
  | PyTorch Version                | PyTorch 2.6.0 with CUDA 12.4 support              | PyTorch 2.6.0 CPU-only build                       |
  | Offload Strategies             | Support `--clm_offload`, `--naive_offload`, `--no_offload` | **Only support `--no_offload`; skip others**      |
  | Environment Variables          | Set `PYTORCH_CUDA_ALLOC_CONF`                      | **Do not set CUDA-related env vars**               |
  | Submodules                     | Compile all including `clm_kernels` (CUDA kernels) | Skip or disable `clm_kernels` compilation          |
  | Training Scripts               | Run all offload modes                              | Run only with `--no_offload`                        |
  | Hardware Requirements          | GPU with ≥24GB VRAM for large-scale, 32GB+ CPU RAM | No GPU needed; maintain CPU RAM and disk requirements |
  | Dataset Decoding & Storage     | Fast local disk; same requirements                 | Same requirements                                  |
  | Testing                       | Include CUDA availability and GPU-specific tests  | Skip CUDA/GPU tests; test CPU-only training        |
  ---
  This adjusted plan ensures your environment setup and workflow are compatible with your CPU-only Linux x86_64 hardware, avoiding GPU dependencies, while preserving dataset handling, model training (with `--no_offload`), and experiment reproducibility.

DOCKERFILE:
  FROM ubuntu:22.04
  ENV DEBIAN_FRONTEND=noninteractive
  ENV LANG=C.UTF-8 LC_ALL=C.UTF-8
  # Install system dependencies
  RUN apt-get update && apt-get install -y --no-install-recommends \
      git \
      curl \
      wget \
      ca-certificates \
      build-essential \
      gcc \
      g++ \
      make \
      python3.10 \
      python3.10-dev \
      python3-pip \
      python3-setuptools \
      python3-venv \
      libgl1-mesa-glx \
      libglib2.0-0 \
      bash \
      && rm -rf /var/lib/apt/lists/*
  # Symlink python3.10 to python and upgrade pip
  RUN update-alternatives --install /usr/bin/python python /usr/bin/python3.10 1 && \
      python -m pip install --upgrade pip setuptools wheel
  # Install Miniconda (latest for Linux x86_64)
  ENV CONDA_DIR=/opt/conda
  RUN wget --quiet https://repo.anaconda.com/miniconda/Miniconda3-latest-Linux-x86_64.sh -O /tmp/miniconda.sh && \
      bash /tmp/miniconda.sh -b -p $CONDA_DIR && \
      rm /tmp/miniconda.sh
  ENV PATH=$CONDA_DIR/bin:$PATH
  # Create conda environment with python 3.10
  RUN $CONDA_DIR/bin/conda create -n clm_gs_cpu python=3.10 -y && \
      $CONDA_DIR/bin/conda clean -afy
  # Install packages inside conda environment using conda run
  RUN conda run -n clm_gs_cpu pip install --upgrade pip setuptools wheel && \
      conda run -n clm_gs_cpu pip install \
        torch==2.6.0+cpu \
        torchvision==0.21.0+cpu \
        torchaudio==2.6.0 \
        --extra-index-url https://download.pytorch.org/whl/cpu && \
      conda run -n clm_gs_cpu pip install \
        tqdm \
        plyfile \
        psutil \
        numba \
        opencv-python \
        scipy \
        matplotlib \
        pandas \
        imageio \
        imageio-ffmpeg \
        requests \
        tabulate \
        black
  WORKDIR /root
  # Clone the main repository with submodules
  RUN git clone --recursive https://github.com/nyu-systems/CLM-GS.git /root/CLM-GS
  WORKDIR /root/CLM-GS
  # Update submodules recursively (in case)
  RUN git submodule update --init --recursive
  # Install CPU-compatible submodules only, skipping clm_kernels (due to CUDA dependency)
  RUN conda run -n clm_gs_cpu pip install --no-build-isolation ./submodules/cpu-adam && \
      conda run -n clm_gs_cpu pip install ./submodules/fast-tsp && \
      conda run -n clm_gs_cpu pip install --no-build-isolation ./submodules/gsplat && \
      conda run -n clm_gs_cpu pip install --no-build-isolation ./submodules/simple-knn
  # Set default shell to bash and start at repo root with conda environment activated
  CMD ["/bin/bash", "-c", ". /opt/conda/etc/profile.d/conda.sh && conda activate clm_gs_cpu && cd /root/CLM-GS && exec /bin/bash"]

  - Notes on offload strategies:  
    - `--clm_offload` **can still be used** in CPU-only mode but CUDA kernels in `clm_kernels` are CUDA-based and require GPU presence; thus, **`--clm_offload` cannot be used on CPU-only systems** because it depends on CUDA and GPU drivers  
    - `--naive_offload` uses CPU pinned memory but also depends on CUDA GPU for data transfer and training; thus, **`--naive_offload` is not applicable without GPU**  
    - **Only `--no_offload` training strategy is feasible and supported on your CPU-only system** (full training on CPU without GPU offloading)  
    - `--no_offload` uses `gsplat` rendering kernels which are native CPU-compatible (compiled submodules support CPU)  
  - Version compatibility requirements:  
    - Python 3.10  
    - PyTorch 2.6.0 CPU-only build  
    - Compatible build tools (gcc/g++, make, python-dev headers) for compiling submodules

  Your hardware environment is Linux x86_64 without an NVIDIA GPU. Consequently, CUDA, GPU drivers, and GPU-accelerated PyTorch builds are not applicable. The plan below is adjusted to fully support CPU-only operation, leveraging CPU training/offload modes, and ensuring compatibility with your hardware. Storage and memory requirements remain important and unchanged. This plan assumes no GPU acceleration and instructs necessary changes accordingly.
  ---
  1. DOWNLOADS NEEDED (ADJUSTED FOR CPU-ONLY):
  - Git (latest stable version) for cloning the repository  
  - Conda (Anaconda or Miniconda) with Python 3.10 environment support  
  - **No NVIDIA GPU driver or CUDA Toolkit installation required** (remove all CUDA 12.4 and related dependencies)  
  - PyTorch 2.6.0 **CPU-only version** (install CPU-only PyTorch build)  
  - Additional Python packages: torchvision 0.21.0, torchaudio 2.6.0 (CPU-only builds if applicable)  
  - Python packages (via pip): tqdm, plyfile, psutil, numba, opencv-python, scipy, matplotlib, pandas, imageio, imageio-ffmpeg, requests, tabulate  
  - Build tools for compiling submodules (e.g., gcc/g++, setuptools) compatible with your Linux OS and x86_64 architecture  
  - Optional: Black code formatter (pip install black)  
  - Adequate local disk storage:  
    - Minimum ~500GB free disk space recommended for MatrixCity BigCity dataset decoded images (as before)  
    - At least 50GB free disk for models/outputs  
    - Fast local disk strongly recommended especially for large datasets (avoid network filesystems)  
  - System memory:  
    - Minimum 32GB RAM recommended for regular experiments  
    - For large-scale datasets (BigCity 102M), 100GB+ CPU RAM recommended for pinned memory allocations  
    - Mip360 and Rubble 4K datasets’ CPU RAM requirements remain unchanged  
  - Optional: bash shell for running example scripts  
  - Notes on offload strategies:  
    - `--clm_offload` **can still be used** in CPU-only mode but CUDA kernels in `clm_kernels` are CUDA-based and require GPU presence; thus, **`--clm_offload` cannot be used on CPU-only systems** because it depends on CUDA and GPU drivers  
    - `--naive_offload` uses CPU pinned memory but also depends on CUDA GPU for data transfer and training; thus, **`--naive_offload` is not applicable without GPU**  
    - **Only `--no_offload` training strategy is feasible and supported on your CPU-only system** (full training on CPU without GPU offloading)  
    - `--no_offload` uses `gsplat` rendering kernels which are native CPU-compatible (compiled submodules support CPU)  
  - Version compatibility requirements:  
    - Python 3.10  
    - PyTorch 2.6.0 CPU-only build  
    - Compatible build tools (gcc/g++, make, python-dev headers) for compiling submodules  
  - Environment variables related to CUDA allocator config (`PYTORCH_CUDA_ALLOC_CONF`) are **not applicable** and should be omitted  
  ---
  2. FILES TO CREATE (UNCHANGED):
  - `.condarc` (optional) for conda configuration  
  - `environment.yml` (optional) with Python 3.10 and all pip packages (adjust PyTorch and torchvision to CPU-only versions)  
  - `README.md`, `LICENSE.txt` as before  
  - Shell scripts for automation (same as before)  
  - Dataset experiment scripts (`release_scripts/bigcity.sh`, `mip360.sh`, `rubble4k.sh`) can be used with `--no_offload` only  
  - Documentation files remain the same  
  - Ensure inclusion and compilation of CPU-compatible submodules (`gsplat`, `clm_kernels` submodule compilation may fail or be skipped due to lack of CUDA; skip or disable `clm_kernels` build)  
  - Ensure `gaussian_model.py` and `engine.py` support `GaussianModelNoOffload` and no GPU dependencies  
  - Omit environment variable config for CUDA allocator  
  - Notes on large disk/memory requirements for datasets remain unchanged

  | Environment Variables          | Set `PYTORCH_CUDA_ALLOC_CONF`                      | **Do not set CUDA-related env vars**               |

  | Training Scripts               | Run all offload modes                              | Run only with `--no_offload`                        |
  | Hardware Requirements          | GPU with ≥24GB VRAM for large-scale, 32GB+ CPU RAM | No GPU needed; maintain CPU RAM and disk requirements |
  | Dataset Decoding & Storage     | Fast local disk; same requirements                 | Same requirements                                  |
  | Testing                       | Include CUDA availability and GPU-specific tests  | Skip CUDA/GPU tests; test CPU-only training        |

DOCKERFILE:
  FROM ubuntu:22.04
  ENV DEBIAN_FRONTEND=noninteractive
  ENV LANG=C.UTF-8 LC_ALL=C.UTF-8
  # Install system dependencies
  RUN apt-get update && apt-get install -y --no-install-recommends \
      git \
      curl \
      wget \
      ca-certificates \
      build-essential \
      gcc \
      g++ \
      make \
      python3.10 \
      python3.10-dev \
      python3-pip \
      python3-setuptools \
      python3-venv \
      libgl1-mesa-glx \
      libglib2.0-0 \
      bash \
      && rm -rf /var/lib/apt/lists/*
  # Symlink python3.10 to python and upgrade pip
  RUN update-alternatives --install /usr/bin/python python /usr/bin/python3.10 1 && \
      python -m pip install --upgrade pip setuptools wheel
  # Install Miniconda (latest for Linux x86_64)
  ENV CONDA_DIR=/opt/conda
  RUN wget --quiet https://repo.anaconda.com/miniconda/Miniconda3-latest-Linux-x86_64.sh -O /tmp/miniconda.sh && \
      bash /tmp/miniconda.sh -b -p $CONDA_DIR && \
      rm /tmp/miniconda.sh
  ENV PATH=$CONDA_DIR/bin:$PATH
  # Create conda environment with python 3.10 using conda executable directly
  RUN $CONDA_DIR/bin/conda create -n clm_gs_cpu python=3.10 -y && \
      $CONDA_DIR/bin/conda clean -afy
  # Install packages inside conda environment using conda run with full conda path
  RUN $CONDA_DIR/bin/conda run -n clm_gs_cpu pip install --upgrade pip setuptools wheel && \
      $CONDA_DIR/bin/conda run -n clm_gs_cpu pip install \
        torch==2.6.0+cpu \
        torchvision==0.21.0+cpu \
        torchaudio==2.6.0 \
        --extra-index-url https://download.pytorch.org/whl/cpu && \
      $CONDA_DIR/bin/conda run -n clm_gs_cpu pip install \
        tqdm \
        plyfile \
        psutil \
        numba \
        opencv-python \
        scipy \
        matplotlib \
        pandas \
        imageio \
        imageio-ffmpeg \
        requests \
        tabulate \
        black
  WORKDIR /root
  # Clone the main repository with submodules
  RUN git clone --recursive https://github.com/nyu-systems/CLM-GS.git /root/CLM-GS
  WORKDIR /root/CLM-GS
  # Update submodules recursively (in case)
  RUN git submodule update --init --recursive
  # Install CPU-compatible submodules only, skipping clm_kernels (due to CUDA dependency)
  RUN $CONDA_DIR/bin/conda run -n clm_gs_cpu pip install --no-build-isolation ./submodules/cpu-adam && \
      $CONDA_DIR/bin/conda run -n clm_gs_cpu pip install ./submodules/fast-tsp && \
      $CONDA_DIR/bin/conda run -n clm_gs_cpu pip install --no-build-isolation ./submodules/gsplat && \
      $CONDA_DIR/bin/conda run -n clm_gs_cpu pip install --no-build-isolation ./submodules/simple-knn
  # Set default shell to bash and start at repo root with conda environment activated
  CMD ["/bin/bash", "-c", ". /opt/conda/etc/profile.d/conda.sh && conda activate clm_gs_cpu && cd /root/CLM-GS && exec /bin/bash"]

  FROM ubuntu:22.04
  ENV DEBIAN_FRONTEND=noninteractive
  ENV LANG=C.UTF-8 LC_ALL=C.UTF-8
  # Install system dependencies
  RUN apt-get update && apt-get install -y --no-install-recommends \
      git \
      curl \
      wget \
      ca-certificates \
      build-essential \
      gcc \
      g++ \
      make \
      python3.10 \
      python3.10-dev \
      python3-pip \
      python3-setuptools \
      python3-venv \
      libgl1-mesa-glx \
      libglib2.0-0 \
      bash \
      && rm -rf /var/lib/apt/lists/*
  # Symlink python3.10 to python and upgrade pip
  RUN update-alternatives --install /usr/bin/python python /usr/bin/python3.10 1 && \
      python -m pip install --upgrade pip setuptools wheel
  # Install Miniconda (latest for Linux x86_64)
  ENV CONDA_DIR=/opt/conda
  RUN wget --quiet https://repo.anaconda.com/miniconda/Miniconda3-latest-Linux-x86_64.sh -O /tmp/miniconda.sh && \
      bash /tmp/miniconda.sh -b -p $CONDA_DIR && \
      rm /tmp/miniconda.sh
  ENV PATH=$CONDA_DIR/bin:$PATH
  # Initialize conda and update conda before environment creation
  RUN $CONDA_DIR/bin/conda init bash && \
      /bin/bash -c "source $CONDA_DIR/etc/profile.d/conda.sh && conda update -n base -c defaults conda -y"
  # Create conda environment with python 3.10 using conda executable directly
  RUN /bin/bash -c "source $CONDA_DIR/etc/profile.d/conda.sh && conda create -n clm_gs_cpu python=3.10 -y && conda clean -afy"
  # Install packages inside conda environment using conda run with full conda path
  RUN /bin/bash -c "source $CONDA_DIR/etc/profile.d/conda.sh && conda run -n clm_gs_cpu pip install --upgrade pip setuptools wheel && \
      conda run -n clm_gs_cpu pip install \
        torch==2.6.0+cpu \
        torchvision==0.21.0+cpu \
        torchaudio==2.6.0 \
        --extra-index-url https://download.pytorch.org/whl/cpu && \
      conda run -n clm_gs_cpu pip install \
        tqdm \
        plyfile \
        psutil \
        numba \
        opencv-python \
        scipy \
        matplotlib \
        pandas \
        imageio \
        imageio-ffmpeg \
        requests \
        tabulate \
        black"
  WORKDIR /root
  # Clone the main repository with submodules
  RUN git clone --recursive https://github.com/nyu-systems/CLM-GS.git /root/CLM-GS
  WORKDIR /root/CLM-GS
  # Update submodules recursively (in case)
  RUN git submodule update --init --recursive
  # Install CPU-compatible submodules only, skipping clm_kernels (due to CUDA dependency)
  RUN /bin/bash -c "source $CONDA_DIR/etc/profile.d/conda.sh && conda run -n clm_gs_cpu pip install --no-build-isolation ./submodules/cpu-adam && \
      conda run -n clm_gs_cpu pip install ./submodules/fast-tsp && \
      conda run -n clm_gs_cpu pip install --no-build-isolation ./submodules/gsplat && \
      conda run -n clm_gs_cpu pip install --no-build-isolation ./submodules/simple-knn"
  # Set default shell to bash and start at repo root with conda environment activated
  CMD ["/bin/bash", "-c", ". /opt/conda/etc/profile.d/conda.sh && conda activate clm_gs_cpu && cd /root/CLM-GS && exec /bin/bash"]

  FROM ubuntu:22.04
  ENV DEBIAN_FRONTEND=noninteractive
  ENV LANG=C.UTF-8 LC_ALL=C.UTF-8
  # Install system dependencies
  RUN apt-get update && apt-get install -y --no-install-recommends \
      git \
      curl \
      wget \
      ca-certificates \
      build-essential \
      gcc \
      g++ \
      make \
      python3.10 \
      python3.10-dev \
      python3-pip \
      python3-setuptools \
      python3-venv \
      libgl1-mesa-glx \
      libglib2.0-0 \
      bash \
      && rm -rf /var/lib/apt/lists/*
  # Symlink python3.10 to python and upgrade pip
  RUN update-alternatives --install /usr/bin/python python /usr/bin/python3.10 1 && \
      python -m pip install --upgrade pip setuptools wheel
  # Install Miniconda (latest for Linux x86_64)
  ENV CONDA_DIR=/opt/conda
  RUN wget --quiet https://repo.anaconda.com/miniconda/Miniconda3-latest-Linux-x86_64.sh -O /tmp/miniconda.sh && \
      bash /tmp/miniconda.sh -b -p $CONDA_DIR && \
      rm /tmp/miniconda.sh
  ENV PATH=$CONDA_DIR/bin:$PATH
  # Update conda base environment without conda init
  RUN $CONDA_DIR/bin/conda update -n base -c defaults conda -y
  # Create conda environment with python 3.10 using conda executable directly
  RUN $CONDA_DIR/bin/conda create -n clm_gs_cpu python=3.10 -y && $CONDA_DIR/bin/conda clean -afy
  # Install packages inside conda environment using conda run with full conda path
  RUN $CONDA_DIR/bin/conda run -n clm_gs_cpu pip install --upgrade pip setuptools wheel && \
      $CONDA_DIR/bin/conda run -n clm_gs_cpu pip install \
        torch==2.6.0+cpu \
        torchvision==0.21.0+cpu \
        torchaudio==2.6.0 \
        --extra-index-url https://download.pytorch.org/whl/cpu && \
      $CONDA_DIR/bin/conda run -n clm_gs_cpu pip install \
        tqdm \
        plyfile \
        psutil \
        numba \
        opencv-python \
        scipy \
        matplotlib \
        pandas \
        imageio \
        imageio-ffmpeg \
        requests \
        tabulate \
        black
  WORKDIR /root
  # Clone the main repository with submodules
  RUN git clone --recursive https://github.com/nyu-systems/CLM-GS.git /root/CLM-GS
  WORKDIR /root/CLM-GS
  # Update submodules recursively (in case)
  RUN git submodule update --init --recursive
  # Install CPU-compatible submodules only, skipping clm_kernels (due to CUDA dependency)
  RUN $CONDA_DIR/bin/conda run -n clm_gs_cpu pip install --no-build-isolation ./submodules/cpu-adam && \
      $CONDA_DIR/bin/conda run -n clm_gs_cpu pip install ./submodules/fast-tsp && \
      $CONDA_DIR/bin/conda run -n clm_gs_cpu pip install --no-build-isolation ./submodules/gsplat && \
      $CONDA_DIR/bin/conda run -n clm_gs_cpu pip install --no-build-isolation ./submodules/simple-knn
  # Set default shell to bash and start at repo root with conda environment activated
  CMD ["/bin/bash", "-c", "source /opt/conda/etc/profile.d/conda.sh && conda activate clm_gs_cpu && cd /root/CLM-GS && exec /bin/bash"]

  **Summary:**  
  Your hardware environment is Linux x86_64 without an NVIDIA GPU. Consequently, CUDA, GPU drivers, and GPU-accelerated PyTorch builds are not applicable. The plan below is adjusted to fully support CPU-only operation, leveraging CPU training/offload modes, and ensuring compatibility with your hardware. Storage and memory requirements remain important and unchanged. This plan assumes no GPU acceleration and instructs necessary changes accordingly.
  ---
  1. DOWNLOADS NEEDED (ADJUSTED FOR CPU-ONLY):
  - Git (latest stable version) for cloning the repository  
  - Conda (Anaconda or Miniconda) with Python 3.10 environment support  
  - **No NVIDIA GPU driver or CUDA Toolkit installation required** (remove all CUDA 12.4 and related dependencies)  
  - PyTorch 2.6.0 **CPU-only version** (install CPU-only PyTorch build)  
  - Additional Python packages: torchvision 0.21.0, torchaudio 2.6.0 (CPU-only builds if applicable)  
  - Python packages (via pip): tqdm, plyfile, psutil, numba, opencv-python, scipy, matplotlib, pandas, imageio, imageio-ffmpeg, requests, tabulate  
  - Build tools for compiling submodules (e.g., gcc/g++, setuptools) compatible with your Linux OS and x86_64 architecture  
  - Optional: Black code formatter (pip install black)  
  - Adequate local disk storage:  
    - Minimum ~500GB free disk space recommended for MatrixCity BigCity dataset decoded images (as before)  
    - At least 50GB free disk for models/outputs  
    - Fast local disk strongly recommended especially for large datasets (avoid network filesystems)  
  - System memory:  
    - Minimum 32GB RAM recommended for regular experiments  
    - For large-scale datasets (BigCity 102M), 100GB+ CPU RAM recommended for pinned memory allocations  
    - Mip360 and Rubble 4K datasets’ CPU RAM requirements remain unchanged  
  - Optional: bash shell for running example scripts  
  - Notes on offload strategies:  
    - `--clm_offload` **can still be used** in CPU-only mode but CUDA kernels in `clm_kernels` are CUDA-based and require GPU presence; thus, **`--clm_offload` cannot be used on CPU-only systems** because it depends on CUDA and GPU drivers  
    - `--naive_offload` uses CPU pinned memory but also depends on CUDA GPU for data transfer and training; thus, **`--naive_offload` is not applicable without GPU**  
    - **Only `--no_offload` training strategy is feasible and supported on your CPU-only system** (full training on CPU without GPU offloading)  
    - `--no_offload` uses `gsplat` rendering kernels which are native CPU-compatible (compiled submodules support CPU)  
  - Version compatibility requirements:  
    - Python 3.10  
    - PyTorch 2.6.0 CPU-only build  
    - Compatible build tools (gcc/g++, make, python-dev headers) for compiling submodules  
  - Environment variables related to CUDA allocator config (`PYTORCH_CUDA_ALLOC_CONF`) are **not applicable** and should be omitted

DOCKERFILE:
  FROM ubuntu:22.04
  ENV DEBIAN_FRONTEND=noninteractive
  ENV LANG=C.UTF-8 LC_ALL=C.UTF-8
  # Install system dependencies
  RUN apt-get update && apt-get install -y --no-install-recommends \
      git \
      curl \
      wget \
      ca-certificates \
      build-essential \
      gcc \
      g++ \
      make \
      python3.10 \
      python3.10-dev \
      python3-pip \
      python3-setuptools \
      python3-venv \
      libgl1-mesa-glx \
      libglib2.0-0 \
      bash \
      && rm -rf /var/lib/apt/lists/*
  # Symlink python3.10 to python and upgrade pip
  RUN update-alternatives --install /usr/bin/python python /usr/bin/python3.10 1 && \
      python -m pip install --upgrade pip setuptools wheel
  # Install Miniconda (latest for Linux x86_64)
  ENV CONDA_DIR=/opt/conda
  RUN wget --quiet https://repo.anaconda.com/miniconda/Miniconda3-latest-Linux-x86_64.sh -O /tmp/miniconda.sh && \
      bash /tmp/miniconda.sh -b -p $CONDA_DIR && \
      rm /tmp/miniconda.sh
  ENV PATH=$CONDA_DIR/bin:$PATH
  # Skip conda update to avoid build failure
  # Create conda environment with python 3.10 using conda executable directly
  RUN $CONDA_DIR/bin/conda create -n clm_gs_cpu python=3.10 -y && $CONDA_DIR/bin/conda clean -afy
  # Install packages inside conda environment using conda run with full conda path
  RUN $CONDA_DIR/bin/conda run -n clm_gs_cpu pip install --upgrade pip setuptools wheel && \
      $CONDA_DIR/bin/conda run -n clm_gs_cpu pip install \
        torch==2.6.0+cpu \
        torchvision==0.21.0+cpu \
        torchaudio==2.6.0 \
        --extra-index-url https://download.pytorch.org/whl/cpu && \
      $CONDA_DIR/bin/conda run -n clm_gs_cpu pip install \
        tqdm \
        plyfile \
        psutil \
        numba \
        opencv-python \
        scipy \
        matplotlib \
        pandas \
        imageio \
        imageio-ffmpeg \
        requests \
        tabulate \
        black
  WORKDIR /root
  # Clone the main repository with submodules
  RUN git clone --recursive https://github.com/nyu-systems/CLM-GS.git /root/CLM-GS
  WORKDIR /root/CLM-GS
  # Update submodules recursively (in case)
  RUN git submodule update --init --recursive
  # Install CPU-compatible submodules only, skipping clm_kernels (due to CUDA dependency)
  RUN $CONDA_DIR/bin/conda run -n clm_gs_cpu pip install --no-build-isolation ./submodules/cpu-adam && \
      $CONDA_DIR/bin/conda run -n clm_gs_cpu pip install ./submodules/fast-tsp && \
      $CONDA_DIR/bin/conda run -n clm_gs_cpu pip install --no-build-isolation ./submodules/gsplat && \
      $CONDA_DIR/bin/conda run -n clm_gs_cpu pip install --no-build-isolation ./submodules/simple-knn
  # Set default shell to bash and start at repo root with conda environment activated
  CMD ["/bin/bash", "-c", "source /opt/conda/etc/profile.d/conda.sh && conda activate clm_gs_cpu && cd /root/CLM-GS && exec /bin/bash"]

PLAN:
  === ADJUSTED ENVIRONMENT SETUP PLAN (for CPU-only Linux x86_64 system) ===
  ---
  **Summary:**  
  Your hardware environment is Linux x86_64 without an NVIDIA GPU. Consequently, CUDA, GPU drivers, and GPU-accelerated PyTorch builds are not applicable. The plan below is adjusted to fully support CPU-only operation, leveraging CPU training/offload modes, and ensuring compatibility with your hardware. Storage and memory requirements remain important and unchanged. This plan assumes no GPU acceleration and instructs necessary changes accordingly.
  ---
  1. DOWNLOADS NEEDED (ADJUSTED FOR CPU-ONLY):
  - Git (latest stable version) for cloning the repository  
  - Conda (Anaconda or Miniconda) with Python 3.10 environment support  
  - **No NVIDIA GPU driver or CUDA Toolkit installation required** (remove all CUDA 12.4 and related dependencies)  
  - PyTorch 2.6.0 **CPU-only version** (install CPU-only PyTorch build)  
  - Additional Python packages: torchvision 0.21.0, torchaudio 2.6.0 (CPU-only builds if applicable)  
  - Python packages (via pip): tqdm, plyfile, psutil, numba, opencv-python, scipy, matplotlib, pandas, imageio, imageio-ffmpeg, requests, tabulate  
  - Build tools for compiling submodules (e.g., gcc/g++, setuptools) compatible with your Linux OS and x86_64 architecture  
  - Optional: Black code formatter (pip install black)  
  - Adequate local disk storage:  
    - Minimum ~500GB free disk space recommended for MatrixCity BigCity dataset decoded images (as before)  
    - At least 50GB free disk for models/outputs  
    - Fast local disk strongly recommended especially for large datasets (avoid network filesystems)  
  - System memory:  
    - Minimum 32GB RAM recommended for regular experiments  
    - For large-scale datasets (BigCity 102M), 100GB+ CPU RAM recommended for pinned memory allocations  
    - Mip360 and Rubble 4K datasets’ CPU RAM requirements remain unchanged  
  - Optional: bash shell for running example scripts  
  - Notes on offload strategies:  
    - `--clm_offload` **can still be used** in CPU-only mode but CUDA kernels in `clm_kernels` are CUDA-based and require GPU presence; thus, **`--clm_offload` cannot be used on CPU-only systems** because it depends on CUDA and GPU drivers  
    - `--naive_offload` uses CPU pinned memory but also depends on CUDA GPU for data transfer and training; thus, **`--naive_offload` is not applicable without GPU**  
    - **Only `--no_offload` training strategy is feasible and supported on your CPU-only system** (full training on CPU without GPU offloading)  
    - `--no_offload` uses `gsplat` rendering kernels which are native CPU-compatible (compiled submodules support CPU)  
  - Version compatibility requirements:  
    - Python 3.10  
    - PyTorch 2.6.0 CPU-only build  
    - Compatible build tools (gcc/g++, make, python-dev headers) for compiling submodules  
  - Environment variables related to CUDA allocator config (`PYTORCH_CUDA_ALLOC_CONF`) are **not applicable** and should be omitted  
  ---
  2. FILES TO CREATE (UNCHANGED):
  - `.condarc` (optional) for conda configuration  
  - `environment.yml` (optional) with Python 3.10 and all pip packages (adjust PyTorch and torchvision to CPU-only versions)  
  - `README.md`, `LICENSE.txt` as before  
  - Shell scripts for automation (same as before)  
  - Dataset experiment scripts (`release_scripts/bigcity.sh`, `mip360.sh`, `rubble4k.sh`) can be used with `--no_offload` only  
  - Documentation files remain the same  
  - Ensure inclusion and compilation of CPU-compatible submodules (`gsplat`, `clm_kernels` submodule compilation may fail or be skipped due to lack of CUDA; skip or disable `clm_kernels` build)  
  - Ensure `gaussian_model.py` and `engine.py` support `GaussianModelNoOffload` and no GPU dependencies  
  - Omit environment variable config for CUDA allocator  
  - Notes on large disk/memory requirements for datasets remain unchanged

  | Training Scripts               | Run all offload modes                              | Run only with `--no_offload`                        |
  | Hardware Requirements          | GPU with ≥24GB VRAM for large-scale, 32GB+ CPU RAM | No GPU needed; maintain CPU RAM and disk requirements |
  | Dataset Decoding & Storage     | Fast local disk; same requirements                 | Same requirements                                  |
  | Testing                       | Include CUDA availability and GPU-specific tests  | Skip CUDA/GPU tests; test CPU-only training        |

DOCKERFILE:
  FROM ubuntu:22.04
  ENV DEBIAN_FRONTEND=noninteractive
  ENV LANG=C.UTF-8 LC_ALL=C.UTF-8
  # Install system dependencies
  RUN apt-get update && apt-get install -y --no-install-recommends \
      git \
      curl \
      wget \
      ca-certificates \
      build-essential \
      gcc \
      g++ \
      make \
      python3.10 \
      python3.10-dev \
      python3-pip \
      python3-setuptools \
      python3-venv \
      libgl1-mesa-glx \
      libglib2.0-0 \
      bash \
      && rm -rf /var/lib/apt/lists/*
  # Symlink python3.10 to python and upgrade pip
  RUN update-alternatives --install /usr/bin/python python /usr/bin/python3.10 1 && \
      python -m pip install --upgrade pip setuptools wheel
  # Install Miniconda (latest for Linux x86_64)
  ENV CONDA_DIR=/opt/conda
  RUN wget --quiet https://repo.anaconda.com/miniconda/Miniconda3-latest-Linux-x86_64.sh -O /tmp/miniconda.sh && \
      bash /tmp/miniconda.sh -b -p $CONDA_DIR && \
      rm /tmp/miniconda.sh
  ENV PATH=$CONDA_DIR/bin:$PATH
  # Initialize conda for bash shell
  RUN /bin/bash -c "source $CONDA_DIR/etc/profile.d/conda.sh && conda init bash"
  SHELL ["/bin/bash", "-c"]
  # Create conda environment with python 3.10 using conda executable directly with conda initialized
  RUN source $CONDA_DIR/etc/profile.d/conda.sh && \
      conda create -n clm_gs_cpu python=3.10 -y && \
      conda clean -afy
  # Install packages inside conda environment using conda run with full conda path
  RUN source $CONDA_DIR/etc/profile.d/conda.sh && conda activate clm_gs_cpu && \
      pip install --upgrade pip setuptools wheel && \
      pip install \
        torch==2.6.0+cpu \
        torchvision==0.21.0+cpu \
        torchaudio==2.6.0 \
        --extra-index-url https://download.pytorch.org/whl/cpu && \
      pip install \
        tqdm \
        plyfile \
        psutil \
        numba \
        opencv-python \
        scipy \
        matplotlib \
        pandas \
        imageio \
        imageio-ffmpeg \
        requests \
        tabulate \
        black
  WORKDIR /root
  # Clone the main repository with submodules
  RUN git clone --recursive https://github.com/nyu-systems/CLM-GS.git /root/CLM-GS
  WORKDIR /root/CLM-GS
  # Update submodules recursively (in case)
  RUN git submodule update --init --recursive
  # Install CPU-compatible submodules only, skipping clm_kernels (due to CUDA dependency)
  RUN source $CONDA_DIR/etc/profile.d/conda.sh && conda activate clm_gs_cpu && \
      pip install --no-build-isolation ./submodules/cpu-adam && \
      pip install ./submodules/fast-tsp && \
      pip install --no-build-isolation ./submodules/gsplat && \
      pip install --no-build-isolation ./submodules/simple-knn
  # Set default shell to bash and start at repo root with conda environment activated
  CMD ["/bin/bash", "-c", "source /opt/conda/etc/profile.d/conda.sh && conda activate clm_gs_cpu && cd /root/CLM-GS && exec /bin/bash"]

  === ADJUSTED ENVIRONMENT SETUP PLAN (for CPU-only Linux x86_64 system) ===
  ---
  **Summary:**  
  Your hardware environment is Linux x86_64 without an NVIDIA GPU. Consequently, CUDA, GPU drivers, and GPU-accelerated PyTorch builds are not applicable. The plan below is adjusted to fully support CPU-only operation, leveraging CPU training/offload modes, and ensuring compatibility with your hardware. Storage and memory requirements remain important and unchanged. This plan assumes no GPU acceleration and instructs necessary changes accordingly.
  ---
  1. DOWNLOADS NEEDED (ADJUSTED FOR CPU-ONLY):
  - Git (latest stable version) for cloning the repository  
  - Conda (Anaconda or Miniconda) with Python 3.10 environment support  
  - **No NVIDIA GPU driver or CUDA Toolkit installation required** (remove all CUDA 12.4 and related dependencies)  
  - PyTorch 2.6.0 **CPU-only version** (install CPU-only PyTorch build)  
  - Additional Python packages: torchvision 0.21.0, torchaudio 2.6.0 (CPU-only builds if applicable)  
  - Python packages (via pip): tqdm, plyfile, psutil, numba, opencv-python, scipy, matplotlib, pandas, imageio, imageio-ffmpeg, requests, tabulate  
  - Build tools for compiling submodules (e.g., gcc/g++, setuptools) compatible with your Linux OS and x86_64 architecture  
  - Optional: Black code formatter (pip install black)  
  - Adequate local disk storage:  
    - Minimum ~500GB free disk space recommended for MatrixCity BigCity dataset decoded images (as before)  
    - At least 50GB free disk for models/outputs  
    - Fast local disk strongly recommended especially for large datasets (avoid network filesystems)  
  - System memory:  
    - Minimum 32GB RAM recommended for regular experiments  
    - For large-scale datasets (BigCity 102M), 100GB+ CPU RAM recommended for pinned memory allocations  
    - Mip360 and Rubble 4K datasets’ CPU RAM requirements remain unchanged  
  - Optional: bash shell for running example scripts  
  - Notes on offload strategies:  
    - `--clm_offload` **can still be used** in CPU-only mode but CUDA kernels in `clm_kernels` are CUDA-based and require GPU presence; thus, **`--clm_offload` cannot be used on CPU-only systems** because it depends on CUDA and GPU drivers  
    - `--naive_offload` uses CPU pinned memory but also depends on CUDA GPU for data transfer and training; thus, **`--naive_offload` is not applicable without GPU**  
    - **Only `--no_offload` training strategy is feasible and supported on your CPU-only system** (full training on CPU without GPU offloading)  
    - `--no_offload` uses `gsplat` rendering kernels which are native CPU-compatible (compiled submodules support CPU)  
  - Version compatibility requirements:  
    - Python 3.10  
    - PyTorch 2.6.0 CPU-only build  
    - Compatible build tools (gcc/g++, make, python-dev headers) for compiling submodules  
  - Environment variables related to CUDA allocator config (`PYTORCH_CUDA_ALLOC_CONF`) are **not applicable** and should be omitted

  Your hardware environment is Linux x86_64 without an NVIDIA GPU. Consequently, CUDA, GPU drivers, and GPU-accelerated PyTorch builds are not applicable. The plan below is adjusted to fully support CPU-only operation, leveraging CPU training/offload modes, and ensuring compatibility with your hardware. Storage and memory requirements remain important and unchanged. This plan assumes no GPU acceleration and instructs necessary changes accordingly.
  ---
  1. DOWNLOADS NEEDED (ADJUSTED FOR CPU-ONLY):
  - Git (latest stable version) for cloning the repository  
  - Conda (Anaconda or Miniconda) with Python 3.10 environment support  
  - **No NVIDIA GPU driver or CUDA Toolkit installation required** (remove all CUDA 12.4 and related dependencies)  
  - PyTorch 2.6.0 **CPU-only version** (install CPU-only PyTorch build)  
  - Additional Python packages: torchvision 0.21.0, torchaudio 2.6.0 (CPU-only builds if applicable)  
  - Python packages (via pip): tqdm, plyfile, psutil, numba, opencv-python, scipy, matplotlib, pandas, imageio, imageio-ffmpeg, requests, tabulate  
  - Build tools for compiling submodules (e.g., gcc/g++, setuptools) compatible with your Linux OS and x86_64 architecture  
  - Optional: Black code formatter (pip install black)  
  - Adequate local disk storage:  
    - Minimum ~500GB free disk space recommended for MatrixCity BigCity dataset decoded images (as before)  
    - At least 50GB free disk for models/outputs  
    - Fast local disk strongly recommended especially for large datasets (avoid network filesystems)  
  - System memory:  
    - Minimum 32GB RAM recommended for regular experiments  
    - For large-scale datasets (BigCity 102M), 100GB+ CPU RAM recommended for pinned memory allocations  
    - Mip360 and Rubble 4K datasets’ CPU RAM requirements remain unchanged  
  - Optional: bash shell for running example scripts  
  - Notes on offload strategies:  
    - `--clm_offload` **can still be used** in CPU-only mode but CUDA kernels in `clm_kernels` are CUDA-based and require GPU presence; thus, **`--clm_offload` cannot be used on CPU-only systems** because it depends on CUDA and GPU drivers  
    - `--naive_offload` uses CPU pinned memory but also depends on CUDA GPU for data transfer and training; thus, **`--naive_offload` is not applicable without GPU**  
    - **Only `--no_offload` training strategy is feasible and supported on your CPU-only system** (full training on CPU without GPU offloading)  
    - `--no_offload` uses `gsplat` rendering kernels which are native CPU-compatible (compiled submodules support CPU)  
  - Version compatibility requirements:  
    - Python 3.10  
    - PyTorch 2.6.0 CPU-only build  
    - Compatible build tools (gcc/g++, make, python-dev headers) for compiling submodules  
  - Environment variables related to CUDA allocator config (`PYTORCH_CUDA_ALLOC_CONF`) are **not applicable** and should be omitted  
  ---
  2. FILES TO CREATE (UNCHANGED):
  - `.condarc` (optional) for conda configuration  
  - `environment.yml` (optional) with Python 3.10 and all pip packages (adjust PyTorch and torchvision to CPU-only versions)  
  - `README.md`, `LICENSE.txt` as before  
  - Shell scripts for automation (same as before)  
  - Dataset experiment scripts (`release_scripts/bigcity.sh`, `mip360.sh`, `rubble4k.sh`) can be used with `--no_offload` only  
  - Documentation files remain the same  
  - Ensure inclusion and compilation of CPU-compatible submodules (`gsplat`, `clm_kernels` submodule compilation may fail or be skipped due to lack of CUDA; skip or disable `clm_kernels` build)  
  - Ensure `gaussian_model.py` and `engine.py` support `GaussianModelNoOffload` and no GPU dependencies  
  - Omit environment variable config for CUDA allocator  
  - Notes on large disk/memory requirements for datasets remain unchanged

  | Aspect                          | Original Plan (GPU)                                | Adjusted Plan (CPU-only)                          |
  |--------------------------------|--------------------------------------------------|--------------------------------------------------|
  | GPU Driver & CUDA Toolkit       | Install CUDA 12.4 & GPU driver                    | **Omit CUDA & GPU driver installation**           |
  | PyTorch Version                | PyTorch 2.6.0 with CUDA 12.4 support              | PyTorch 2.6.0 CPU-only build                       |
  | Offload Strategies             | Support `--clm_offload`, `--naive_offload`, `--no_offload` | **Only support `--no_offload`; skip others**      |
  | Environment Variables          | Set `PYTORCH_CUDA_ALLOC_CONF`                      | **Do not set CUDA-related env vars**               |
  | Submodules                     | Compile all including `clm_kernels` (CUDA kernels) | Skip or disable `clm_kernels` compilation          |
  | Training Scripts               | Run all offload modes                              | Run only with `--no_offload`                        |
  | Hardware Requirements          | GPU with ≥24GB VRAM for large-scale, 32GB+ CPU RAM | No GPU needed; maintain CPU RAM and disk requirements |
  | Dataset Decoding & Storage     | Fast local disk; same requirements                 | Same requirements                                  |
  | Testing                       | Include CUDA availability and GPU-specific tests  | Skip CUDA/GPU tests; test CPU-only training        |

DOCKERFILE:
  FROM ubuntu:22.04
  ENV DEBIAN_FRONTEND=noninteractive
  ENV LANG=C.UTF-8 LC_ALL=C.UTF-8
  # Install system dependencies
  RUN apt-get update && apt-get install -y --no-install-recommends \
      git \
      curl \
      wget \
      ca-certificates \
      build-essential \
      gcc \
      g++ \
      make \
      python3.10 \
      python3.10-dev \
      python3-pip \
      python3-setuptools \
      python3-venv \
      libgl1-mesa-glx \
      libglib2.0-0 \
      bash \
      && rm -rf /var/lib/apt/lists/*
  # Symlink python3.10 to python and upgrade pip
  RUN update-alternatives --install /usr/bin/python python /usr/bin/python3.10 1 && \
      python -m pip install --upgrade pip setuptools wheel
  # Install Miniconda (latest for Linux x86_64)
  ENV CONDA_DIR=/opt/conda
  RUN wget --quiet https://repo.anaconda.com/miniconda/Miniconda3-latest-Linux-x86_64.sh -O /tmp/miniconda.sh && \
      bash /tmp/miniconda.sh -b -p $CONDA_DIR && \
      rm /tmp/miniconda.sh
  ENV PATH=$CONDA_DIR/bin:$PATH
  # Initialize conda
  SHELL ["/bin/bash", "-c"]
  RUN source $CONDA_DIR/etc/profile.d/conda.sh && \
      conda create -n clm_gs_cpu python=3.10 -y && \
      conda clean -afy
  # Install packages inside conda environment using conda run
  RUN source $CONDA_DIR/etc/profile.d/conda.sh && \
      conda run -n clm_gs_cpu pip install --upgrade pip setuptools wheel && \
      conda run -n clm_gs_cpu pip install \
        torch==2.6.0+cpu \
        torchvision==0.21.0+cpu \
        torchaudio==2.6.0 \
        --extra-index-url https://download.pytorch.org/whl/cpu && \
      conda run -n clm_gs_cpu pip install \
        tqdm \
        plyfile \
        psutil \
        numba \
        opencv-python \
        scipy \
        matplotlib \
        pandas \
        imageio \
        imageio-ffmpeg \
        requests \
        tabulate \
        black
  WORKDIR /root
  # Clone the main repository with submodules
  RUN git clone --recursive https://github.com/nyu-systems/CLM-GS.git /root/CLM-GS
  WORKDIR /root/CLM-GS
  # Update submodules recursively (in case)
  RUN git submodule update --init --recursive
  # Install CPU-compatible submodules only, skipping clm_kernels (due to CUDA dependency)
  RUN source $CONDA_DIR/etc/profile.d/conda.sh && \
      conda run -n clm_gs_cpu pip install --no-build-isolation ./submodules/cpu-adam && \
      conda run -n clm_gs_cpu pip install ./submodules/fast-tsp && \
      conda run -n clm_gs_cpu pip install --no-build-isolation ./submodules/gsplat && \
      conda run -n clm_gs_cpu pip install --no-build-isolation ./submodules/simple-knn
  # Set default shell to bash and start at repo root with conda environment activated
  CMD ["/bin/bash", "-c", "source /opt/conda/etc/profile.d/conda.sh && conda activate clm_gs_cpu && cd /root/CLM-GS && exec /bin/bash"]

  | Dataset Decoding & Storage     | Fast local disk; same requirements                 | Same requirements                                  |
  | Testing                       | Include CUDA availability and GPU-specific tests  | Skip CUDA/GPU tests; test CPU-only training        |

  FROM ubuntu:22.04
  ENV DEBIAN_FRONTEND=noninteractive
  ENV LANG=C.UTF-8 LC_ALL=C.UTF-8
  # Install system dependencies
  RUN apt-get update && apt-get install -y --no-install-recommends \
      git \
      curl \
      wget \
      ca-certificates \
      build-essential \
      gcc \
      g++ \
      make \
      python3.10 \
      python3.10-dev \
      python3-pip \
      python3-setuptools \
      python3-venv \
      libgl1-mesa-glx \
      libglib2.0-0 \
      bash \
      && rm -rf /var/lib/apt/lists/*
  # Symlink python3.10 to python and upgrade pip
  RUN update-alternatives --install /usr/bin/python python /usr/bin/python3.10 1 && \
      python -m pip install --upgrade pip setuptools wheel
  # Install Miniconda (latest for Linux x86_64)
  ENV CONDA_DIR=/opt/conda
  RUN wget --quiet https://repo.anaconda.com/miniconda/Miniconda3-latest-Linux-x86_64.sh -O /tmp/miniconda.sh && \
      bash /tmp/miniconda.sh -b -p $CONDA_DIR && \
      rm /tmp/miniconda.sh
  ENV PATH=$CONDA_DIR/bin:$PATH
  # Initialize conda and create environment in one RUN command
  SHELL ["/bin/bash", "-c"]
  RUN source $CONDA_DIR/etc/profile.d/conda.sh && \
      conda init bash && \
      conda create -n clm_gs_cpu python=3.10 -y && \
      conda clean -afy
  # Install packages inside conda environment using conda run
  RUN source $CONDA_DIR/etc/profile.d/conda.sh && \
      conda run -n clm_gs_cpu pip install --upgrade pip setuptools wheel && \
      conda run -n clm_gs_cpu pip install \
        torch==2.6.0+cpu \
        torchvision==0.21.0+cpu \
        torchaudio==2.6.0 \
        --extra-index-url https://download.pytorch.org/whl/cpu && \
      conda run -n clm_gs_cpu pip install \
        tqdm \
        plyfile \
        psutil \
        numba \
        opencv-python \
        scipy \
        matplotlib \
        pandas \
        imageio \
        imageio-ffmpeg \
        requests \
        tabulate \
        black
  WORKDIR /root
  # Clone the main repository with submodules
  RUN git clone --recursive https://github.com/nyu-systems/CLM-GS.git /root/CLM-GS
  WORKDIR /root/CLM-GS
  # Update submodules recursively (in case)
  RUN git submodule update --init --recursive
  # Install CPU-compatible submodules only, skipping clm_kernels (due to CUDA dependency)
  RUN source $CONDA_DIR/etc/profile.d/conda.sh && \
      conda run -n clm_gs_cpu pip install --no-build-isolation ./submodules/cpu-adam && \
      conda run -n clm_gs_cpu pip install ./submodules/fast-tsp && \
      conda run -n clm_gs_cpu pip install --no-build-isolation ./submodules/gsplat && \
      conda run -n clm_gs_cpu pip install --no-build-isolation ./submodules/simple-knn
  # Set default shell to bash and start at repo root with conda environment activated
  CMD ["/bin/bash", "-c", "source /opt/conda/etc/profile.d/conda.sh && conda activate clm_gs_cpu && cd /root/CLM-GS && exec /bin/bash"]

    - `--no_offload` uses `gsplat` rendering kernels which are native CPU-compatible (compiled submodules support CPU)

  FROM ubuntu:22.04
  ENV DEBIAN_FRONTEND=noninteractive
  ENV LANG=C.UTF-8 LC_ALL=C.UTF-8
  # Install system dependencies
  RUN apt-get update && apt-get install -y --no-install-recommends \
      git \
      curl \
      wget \
      ca-certificates \
      build-essential \
      gcc \
      g++ \
      make \
      python3.10 \
      python3.10-dev \
      python3-pip \
      python3-setuptools \
      python3-venv \
      libgl1-mesa-glx \
      libglib2.0-0 \
      bash \
      && rm -rf /var/lib/apt/lists/*
  # Symlink python3.10 to python and upgrade pip
  RUN update-alternatives --install /usr/bin/python python /usr/bin/python3.10 1 && \
      python -m pip install --upgrade pip setuptools wheel
  # Install Miniconda (latest for Linux x86_64)
  ENV CONDA_DIR=/opt/conda
  RUN wget --quiet https://repo.anaconda.com/miniconda/Miniconda3-latest-Linux-x86_64.sh -O /tmp/miniconda.sh && \
      bash /tmp/miniconda.sh -b -p $CONDA_DIR && \
      rm /tmp/miniconda.sh
  ENV PATH=$CONDA_DIR/bin:$PATH
  # Create conda environment without activating shell
  RUN conda create -n clm_gs_cpu python=3.10 -y && conda clean -afy
  # Upgrade pip and install packages inside conda environment using conda run
  RUN conda run -n clm_gs_cpu pip install --upgrade pip setuptools wheel && \
      conda run -n clm_gs_cpu pip install \
        torch==2.6.0+cpu \
        torchvision==0.21.0+cpu \
        torchaudio==2.6.0 \
        --extra-index-url https://download.pytorch.org/whl/cpu && \
      conda run -n clm_gs_cpu pip install \
        tqdm \
        plyfile \
        psutil \
        numba \
        opencv-python \
        scipy \
        matplotlib \
        pandas \
        imageio \
        imageio-ffmpeg \
        requests \
        tabulate \
        black
  WORKDIR /root
  # Clone the main repository with submodules
  RUN git clone --recursive https://github.com/nyu-systems/CLM-GS.git /root/CLM-GS
  WORKDIR /root/CLM-GS
  # Update submodules recursively (in case)
  RUN git submodule update --init --recursive
  # Install CPU-compatible submodules only, skipping clm_kernels (due to CUDA dependency)
  RUN conda run -n clm_gs_cpu pip install --no-build-isolation ./submodules/cpu-adam && \
      conda run -n clm_gs_cpu pip install ./submodules/fast-tsp && \
      conda run -n clm_gs_cpu pip install --no-build-isolation ./submodules/gsplat && \
      conda run -n clm_gs_cpu pip install --no-build-isolation ./submodules/simple-knn
  # Set default shell to bash and start at repo root with conda environment activated
  CMD ["/bin/bash", "-c", "source /opt/conda/etc/profile.d/conda.sh && conda activate clm_gs_cpu && cd /root/CLM-GS && exec /bin/bash"]

  ---
  **Summary:**  
  Your hardware environment is Linux x86_64 without an NVIDIA GPU. Consequently, CUDA, GPU drivers, and GPU-accelerated PyTorch builds are not applicable. The plan below is adjusted to fully support CPU-only operation, leveraging CPU training/offload modes, and ensuring compatibility with your hardware. Storage and memory requirements remain important and unchanged. This plan assumes no GPU acceleration and instructs necessary changes accordingly.
  ---
  1. DOWNLOADS NEEDED (ADJUSTED FOR CPU-ONLY):
  - Git (latest stable version) for cloning the repository  
  - Conda (Anaconda or Miniconda) with Python 3.10 environment support  
  - **No NVIDIA GPU driver or CUDA Toolkit installation required** (remove all CUDA 12.4 and related dependencies)  
  - PyTorch 2.6.0 **CPU-only version** (install CPU-only PyTorch build)  
  - Additional Python packages: torchvision 0.21.0, torchaudio 2.6.0 (CPU-only builds if applicable)  
  - Python packages (via pip): tqdm, plyfile, psutil, numba, opencv-python, scipy, matplotlib, pandas, imageio, imageio-ffmpeg, requests, tabulate  
  - Build tools for compiling submodules (e.g., gcc/g++, setuptools) compatible with your Linux OS and x86_64 architecture  
  - Optional: Black code formatter (pip install black)  
  - Adequate local disk storage:  
    - Minimum ~500GB free disk space recommended for MatrixCity BigCity dataset decoded images (as before)  
    - At least 50GB free disk for models/outputs  
    - Fast local disk strongly recommended especially for large datasets (avoid network filesystems)  
  - System memory:  
    - Minimum 32GB RAM recommended for regular experiments  
    - For large-scale datasets (BigCity 102M), 100GB+ CPU RAM recommended for pinned memory allocations  
    - Mip360 and Rubble 4K datasets’ CPU RAM requirements remain unchanged  
  - Optional: bash shell for running example scripts  
  - Notes on offload strategies:  
    - `--clm_offload` **can still be used** in CPU-only mode but CUDA kernels in `clm_kernels` are CUDA-based and require GPU presence; thus, **`--clm_offload` cannot be used on CPU-only systems** because it depends on CUDA and GPU drivers  
    - `--naive_offload` uses CPU pinned memory but also depends on CUDA GPU for data transfer and training; thus, **`--naive_offload` is not applicable without GPU**  
    - **Only `--no_offload` training strategy is feasible and supported on your CPU-only system** (full training on CPU without GPU offloading)  
    - `--no_offload` uses `gsplat` rendering kernels which are native CPU-compatible (compiled submodules support CPU)  
  - Version compatibility requirements:  
    - Python 3.10  
    - PyTorch 2.6.0 CPU-only build  
    - Compatible build tools (gcc/g++, make, python-dev headers) for compiling submodules  
  - Environment variables related to CUDA allocator config (`PYTORCH_CUDA_ALLOC_CONF`) are **not applicable** and should be omitted

  FROM ubuntu:22.04
  ENV DEBIAN_FRONTEND=noninteractive
  ENV LANG=C.UTF-8 LC_ALL=C.UTF-8
  # Install system dependencies
  RUN apt-get update && apt-get install -y --no-install-recommends \
      git \
      curl \
      wget \
      ca-certificates \
      build-essential \
      gcc \
      g++ \
      make \
      python3.10 \
      python3.10-dev \
      python3-pip \
      python3-setuptools \
      python3-venv \
      libgl1-mesa-glx \
      libglib2.0-0 \
      bash \
      && rm -rf /var/lib/apt/lists/*
  # Symlink python3.10 to python and upgrade pip
  RUN update-alternatives --install /usr/bin/python python /usr/bin/python3.10 1 && \
      python -m pip install --upgrade pip setuptools wheel
  # Install Miniconda (latest for Linux x86_64)
  ENV CONDA_DIR=/opt/conda
  RUN wget --quiet https://repo.anaconda.com/miniconda/Miniconda3-latest-Linux-x86_64.sh -O /tmp/miniconda.sh && \
      bash /tmp/miniconda.sh -b -p $CONDA_DIR && \
      rm /tmp/miniconda.sh
  ENV PATH=$CONDA_DIR/bin:$PATH
  # Initialize conda and create environment inside bash shell
  RUN /bin/bash -c "source $CONDA_DIR/etc/profile.d/conda.sh && conda create -n clm_gs_cpu python=3.10 -y && conda clean -afy"
  # Upgrade pip and install packages inside conda environment using conda run
  RUN conda run -n clm_gs_cpu pip install --upgrade pip setuptools wheel && \
      conda run -n clm_gs_cpu pip install \
        torch==2.6.0+cpu \
        torchvision==0.21.0+cpu \
        torchaudio==2.6.0 \
        --extra-index-url https://download.pytorch.org/whl/cpu && \
      conda run -n clm_gs_cpu pip install \
        tqdm \
        plyfile \
        psutil \
        numba \
        opencv-python \
        scipy \
        matplotlib \
        pandas \
        imageio \
        imageio-ffmpeg \
        requests \
        tabulate \
        black
  WORKDIR /root
  # Clone the main repository with submodules
  RUN git clone --recursive https://github.com/nyu-systems/CLM-GS.git /root/CLM-GS
  WORKDIR /root/CLM-GS
  # Update submodules recursively (in case)
  RUN git submodule update --init --recursive
  # Install CPU-compatible submodules only, skipping clm_kernels (due to CUDA dependency)
  RUN conda run -n clm_gs_cpu pip install --no-build-isolation ./submodules/cpu-adam && \
      conda run -n clm_gs_cpu pip install ./submodules/fast-tsp && \
      conda run -n clm_gs_cpu pip install --no-build-isolation ./submodules/gsplat && \
      conda run -n clm_gs_cpu pip install --no-build-isolation ./submodules/simple-knn
  # Set default shell to bash and start at repo root with conda environment activated
  CMD ["/bin/bash", "-c", "source /opt/conda/etc/profile.d/conda.sh && conda activate clm_gs_cpu && cd /root/CLM-GS && exec /bin/bash"]
