PLAN:
  === ADJUSTED ENVIRONMENT SETUP PLAN (for CPU-only Linux x86_64 system) ===
  ---
  **Summary:**  
  Your hardware environment is Linux x86_64 without an NVIDIA GPU. Consequently, CUDA, GPU drivers, and GPU-accelerated PyTorch builds are not applicable. The plan below is adjusted to fully support CPU-only operation, leveraging CPU training/offload modes, and ensuring compatibility with your hardware. Storage and memory requirements remain important and unchanged. This plan assumes no GPU acceleration and instructs necessary changes accordingly.
  ---
  1. DOWNLOADS NEEDED (ADJUSTED FOR CPU-ONLY):
  - Git (latest stable version) for cloning the repository  
  - Conda (Anaconda or Miniconda) with Python 3.10 environment support  
  - **No NVIDIA GPU driver or CUDA Toolkit installation required** (remove all CUDA 12.4 and related dependencies)  
  - PyTorch 2.6.0 **CPU-only version** (install CPU-only PyTorch build)  
  - Additional Python packages: torchvision 0.21.0, torchaudio 2.6.0 (CPU-only builds if applicable)  
  - Python packages (via pip): tqdm, plyfile, psutil, numba, opencv-python, scipy, matplotlib, pandas, imageio, imageio-ffmpeg, requests, tabulate  
  - Build tools for compiling submodules (e.g., gcc/g++, setuptools) compatible with your Linux OS and x86_64 architecture  
  - Optional: Black code formatter (pip install black)  
  - Adequate local disk storage:  
    - Minimum ~500GB free disk space recommended for MatrixCity BigCity dataset decoded images (as before)  
    - At least 50GB free disk for models/outputs  
    - Fast local disk strongly recommended especially for large datasets (avoid network filesystems)  
  - System memory:  
    - Minimum 32GB RAM recommended for regular experiments  
    - For large-scale datasets (BigCity 102M), 100GB+ CPU RAM recommended for pinned memory allocations  
    - Mip360 and Rubble 4K datasets’ CPU RAM requirements remain unchanged  
  - Optional: bash shell for running example scripts  
  - Notes on offload strategies:  
    - `--clm_offload` **can still be used** in CPU-only mode but CUDA kernels in `clm_kernels` are CUDA-based and require GPU presence; thus, **`--clm_offload` cannot be used on CPU-only systems** because it depends on CUDA and GPU drivers  
    - `--naive_offload` uses CPU pinned memory but also depends on CUDA GPU for data transfer and training; thus, **`--naive_offload` is not applicable without GPU**  
    - **Only `--no_offload` training strategy is feasible and supported on your CPU-only system** (full training on CPU without GPU offloading)  
    - `--no_offload` uses `gsplat` rendering kernels which are native CPU-compatible (compiled submodules support CPU)  
  - Version compatibility requirements:  
    - Python 3.10  
    - PyTorch 2.6.0 CPU-only build  
    - Compatible build tools (gcc/g++, make, python-dev headers) for compiling submodules  
  - Environment variables related to CUDA allocator config (`PYTORCH_CUDA_ALLOC_CONF`) are **not applicable** and should be omitted  
  ---
  2. FILES TO CREATE (UNCHANGED):
  - `.condarc` (optional) for conda configuration  
  - `environment.yml` (optional) with Python 3.10 and all pip packages (adjust PyTorch and torchvision to CPU-only versions)

  - Documentation files remain the same

  - Ensure `gaussian_model.py` and `engine.py` support `GaussianModelNoOffload` and no GPU dependencies

DOCKERFILE:
  FROM ubuntu:22.04
  ENV DEBIAN_FRONTEND=noninteractive
  ENV LANG=C.UTF-8 LC_ALL=C.UTF-8
  # Install system dependencies
  RUN apt-get update && apt-get install -y --no-install-recommends \
      git \
      curl \
      wget \
      ca-certificates \
      build-essential \
      gcc \
      g++ \
      make \
      python3.10 \
      python3.10-dev \
      python3-pip \
      python3-setuptools \
      python3-venv \
      libgl1-mesa-glx \
      libglib2.0-0 \
      bash \
      && rm -rf /var/lib/apt/lists/*
  # Symlink python3.10 to python and upgrade pip
  RUN update-alternatives --install /usr/bin/python python /usr/bin/python3.10 1 && \
      python -m pip install --upgrade pip setuptools wheel
  # Install Miniconda (latest for Linux x86_64)
  ENV CONDA_DIR=/opt/conda
  RUN wget --quiet https://repo.anaconda.com/miniconda/Miniconda3-latest-Linux-x86_64.sh -O /tmp/miniconda.sh && \
      bash /tmp/miniconda.sh -b -p $CONDA_DIR && \
      rm /tmp/miniconda.sh
  ENV PATH=$CONDA_DIR/bin:$PATH
  # Initialize conda base environment and create clm_gs_cpu environment without subshell
  RUN conda init bash && \
      conda create -n clm_gs_cpu python=3.10 -y && \
      conda clean -afy
  # Upgrade pip and install packages inside conda environment using conda run
  RUN conda run -n clm_gs_cpu pip install --upgrade pip setuptools wheel && \
      conda run -n clm_gs_cpu pip install \
        torch==2.6.0+cpu \
        torchvision==0.21.0+cpu \
        torchaudio==2.6.0 \
        --extra-index-url https://download.pytorch.org/whl/cpu && \
      conda run -n clm_gs_cpu pip install \
        tqdm \
        plyfile \
        psutil \
        numba \
        opencv-python \
        scipy \
        matplotlib \
        pandas \
        imageio \
        imageio-ffmpeg \
        requests \
        tabulate \
        black
  WORKDIR /root
  # Clone the main repository with submodules
  RUN git clone --recursive https://github.com/nyu-systems/CLM-GS.git /root/CLM-GS
  WORKDIR /root/CLM-GS
  # Update submodules recursively (in case)
  RUN git submodule update --init --recursive
  # Install CPU-compatible submodules only, skipping clm_kernels (due to CUDA dependency)
  RUN conda run -n clm_gs_cpu pip install --no-build-isolation ./submodules/cpu-adam && \
      conda run -n clm_gs_cpu pip install ./submodules/fast-tsp && \
      conda run -n clm_gs_cpu pip install --no-build-isolation ./submodules/gsplat && \
      conda run -n clm_gs_cpu pip install --no-build-isolation ./submodules/simple-knn
  # Set default shell to bash and start at repo root with conda environment activated
  CMD ["/bin/bash", "-c", "source /opt/conda/etc/profile.d/conda.sh && conda activate clm_gs_cpu && cd /root/CLM-GS && exec /bin/bash"]

  **Summary:**  
  Your hardware environment is Linux x86_64 without an NVIDIA GPU. Consequently, CUDA, GPU drivers, and GPU-accelerated PyTorch builds are not applicable. The plan below is adjusted to fully support CPU-only operation, leveraging CPU training/offload modes, and ensuring compatibility with your hardware. Storage and memory requirements remain important and unchanged. This plan assumes no GPU acceleration and instructs necessary changes accordingly.
  ---
  1. DOWNLOADS NEEDED (ADJUSTED FOR CPU-ONLY):
  - Git (latest stable version) for cloning the repository  
  - Conda (Anaconda or Miniconda) with Python 3.10 environment support  
  - **No NVIDIA GPU driver or CUDA Toolkit installation required** (remove all CUDA 12.4 and related dependencies)  
  - PyTorch 2.6.0 **CPU-only version** (install CPU-only PyTorch build)  
  - Additional Python packages: torchvision 0.21.0, torchaudio 2.6.0 (CPU-only builds if applicable)  
  - Python packages (via pip): tqdm, plyfile, psutil, numba, opencv-python, scipy, matplotlib, pandas, imageio, imageio-ffmpeg, requests, tabulate  
  - Build tools for compiling submodules (e.g., gcc/g++, setuptools) compatible with your Linux OS and x86_64 architecture

    - Minimum ~500GB free disk space recommended for MatrixCity BigCity dataset decoded images (as before)  
    - At least 50GB free disk for models/outputs  
    - Fast local disk strongly recommended especially for large datasets (avoid network filesystems)  
  - System memory:  
    - Minimum 32GB RAM recommended for regular experiments  
    - For large-scale datasets (BigCity 102M), 100GB+ CPU RAM recommended for pinned memory allocations  
    - Mip360 and Rubble 4K datasets’ CPU RAM requirements remain unchanged  
  - Optional: bash shell for running example scripts  
  - Notes on offload strategies:  
    - `--clm_offload` **can still be used** in CPU-only mode but CUDA kernels in `clm_kernels` are CUDA-based and require GPU presence; thus, **`--clm_offload` cannot be used on CPU-only systems** because it depends on CUDA and GPU drivers  
    - `--naive_offload` uses CPU pinned memory but also depends on CUDA GPU for data transfer and training; thus, **`--naive_offload` is not applicable without GPU**  
    - **Only `--no_offload` training strategy is feasible and supported on your CPU-only system** (full training on CPU without GPU offloading)  
    - `--no_offload` uses `gsplat` rendering kernels which are native CPU-compatible (compiled submodules support CPU)  
  - Version compatibility requirements:  
    - Python 3.10  
    - PyTorch 2.6.0 CPU-only build  
    - Compatible build tools (gcc/g++, make, python-dev headers) for compiling submodules  
  - Environment variables related to CUDA allocator config (`PYTORCH_CUDA_ALLOC_CONF`) are **not applicable** and should be omitted

    - Minimum ~500GB free disk space recommended for MatrixCity BigCity dataset decoded images (as before)  
    - At least 50GB free disk for models/outputs  
    - Fast local disk strongly recommended especially for large datasets (avoid network filesystems)  
  - System memory:  
    - Minimum 32GB RAM recommended for regular experiments  
    - For large-scale datasets (BigCity 102M), 100GB+ CPU RAM recommended for pinned memory allocations  
    - Mip360 and Rubble 4K datasets’ CPU RAM requirements remain unchanged  
  - Optional: bash shell for running example scripts  
  - Notes on offload strategies:  
    - `--clm_offload` **can still be used** in CPU-only mode but CUDA kernels in `clm_kernels` are CUDA-based and require GPU presence; thus, **`--clm_offload` cannot be used on CPU-only systems** because it depends on CUDA and GPU drivers  
    - `--naive_offload` uses CPU pinned memory but also depends on CUDA GPU for data transfer and training; thus, **`--naive_offload` is not applicable without GPU**  
    - **Only `--no_offload` training strategy is feasible and supported on your CPU-only system** (full training on CPU without GPU offloading)  
    - `--no_offload` uses `gsplat` rendering kernels which are native CPU-compatible (compiled submodules support CPU)  
  - Version compatibility requirements:  
    - Python 3.10  
    - PyTorch 2.6.0 CPU-only build  
    - Compatible build tools (gcc/g++, make, python-dev headers) for compiling submodules  
  - Environment variables related to CUDA allocator config (`PYTORCH_CUDA_ALLOC_CONF`) are **not applicable** and should be omitted  
  ---
  2. FILES TO CREATE (UNCHANGED):
  - `.condarc` (optional) for conda configuration  
  - `environment.yml` (optional) with Python 3.10 and all pip packages (adjust PyTorch and torchvision to CPU-only versions)  
  - `README.md`, `LICENSE.txt` as before  
  - Shell scripts for automation (same as before)  
  - Dataset experiment scripts (`release_scripts/bigcity.sh`, `mip360.sh`, `rubble4k.sh`) can be used with `--no_offload` only  
  - Documentation files remain the same  
  - Ensure inclusion and compilation of CPU-compatible submodules (`gsplat`, `clm_kernels` submodule compilation may fail or be skipped due to lack of CUDA; skip or disable `clm_kernels` build)  
  - Ensure `gaussian_model.py` and `engine.py` support `GaussianModelNoOffload` and no GPU dependencies  
  - Omit environment variable config for CUDA allocator  
  - Notes on large disk/memory requirements for datasets remain unchanged

  | Testing                       | Include CUDA availability and GPU-specific tests  | Skip CUDA/GPU tests; test CPU-only training        |

      git \
      curl \
      wget \
      ca-certificates \
      build-essential \
      gcc \
      g++ \
      make \
      python3.10 \
      python3.10-dev \
      python3-pip \
      python3-setuptools \
      python3-venv \
      libgl1-mesa-glx \
      libglib2.0-0 \
      bash \
      && rm -rf /var/lib/apt/lists/*
  # Symlink python3.10 to python and upgrade pip
  RUN update-alternatives --install /usr/bin/python python /usr/bin/python3.10 1 && \
      python -m pip install --upgrade pip setuptools wheel
  # Install Miniconda (latest for Linux x86_64)
  ENV CONDA_DIR=/opt/conda
  RUN wget --quiet https://repo.anaconda.com/miniconda/Miniconda3-latest-Linux-x86_64.sh -O /tmp/miniconda.sh && \
      bash /tmp/miniconda.sh -b -p $CONDA_DIR && \
      rm /tmp/miniconda.sh
  ENV PATH=$CONDA_DIR/bin:$PATH
  # Use bash shell for conda initialization and environment creation
  SHELL ["/bin/bash", "-c"]
  # Initialize conda for bash and create conda environment clm_gs_cpu with python 3.10
  RUN source $CONDA_DIR/etc/profile.d/conda.sh && \
      conda init bash && \
      conda create -n clm_gs_cpu python=3.10 -y && \
      conda clean -afy
  # Upgrade pip and install packages inside conda environment using conda run
  RUN source $CONDA_DIR/etc/profile.d/conda.sh && \
      conda activate clm_gs_cpu && \
      pip install --upgrade pip setuptools wheel && \
      pip install \
        torch==2.6.0+cpu \
        torchvision==0.21.0+cpu \
        torchaudio==2.6.0 \
        --extra-index-url https://download.pytorch.org/whl/cpu && \
      pip install \
        tqdm \
        plyfile \
        psutil \
        numba \
        opencv-python \
        scipy \
        matplotlib \
        pandas \
        imageio \
        imageio-ffmpeg \
        requests \
        tabulate \
        black
  WORKDIR /root
  # Clone the main repository with submodules
  RUN git clone --recursive https://github.com/nyu-systems/CLM-GS.git /root/CLM-GS
  WORKDIR /root/CLM-GS
  # Update submodules recursively (in case)
  RUN git submodule update --init --recursive
  # Install CPU-compatible submodules only, skipping clm_kernels (due to CUDA dependency)
  RUN source $CONDA_DIR/etc/profile.d/conda.sh && \
      conda activate clm_gs_cpu && \
      pip install --no-build-isolation ./submodules/cpu-adam && \
      pip install ./submodules/fast-tsp && \
      pip install --no-build-isolation ./submodules/gsplat && \
      pip install --no-build-isolation ./submodules/simple-knn
  # Set default shell to bash and start at repo root with conda environment activated
  CMD ["/bin/bash", "-c", "source /opt/conda/etc/profile.d/conda.sh && conda activate clm_gs_cpu && cd /root/CLM-GS && exec /bin/bash"]

  FROM ubuntu:22.04
  ENV DEBIAN_FRONTEND=noninteractive
  ENV LANG=C.UTF-8 LC_ALL=C.UTF-8
  # Install system dependencies
  RUN apt-get update && apt-get install -y --no-install-recommends \
      git \
      curl \
      wget \
      ca-certificates \
      build-essential \
      gcc \
      g++ \
      make \
      python3.10 \
      python3.10-dev \
      python3-pip \
      python3-setuptools \
      python3-venv \
      libgl1-mesa-glx \
      libglib2.0-0 \
      bash \
      && rm -rf /var/lib/apt/lists/*
  # Symlink python3.10 to python and upgrade pip
  RUN update-alternatives --install /usr/bin/python python /usr/bin/python3.10 1 && \
      python -m pip install --upgrade pip setuptools wheel
  # Install Miniconda (latest for Linux x86_64)
  ENV CONDA_DIR=/opt/conda
  RUN wget --quiet https://repo.anaconda.com/miniconda/Miniconda3-latest-Linux-x86_64.sh -O /tmp/miniconda.sh && \
      bash /tmp/miniconda.sh -b -p $CONDA_DIR && \
      rm /tmp/miniconda.sh
  ENV PATH=$CONDA_DIR/bin:$PATH
  # Create conda environment clm_gs_cpu with python 3.10 without using conda init
  RUN $CONDA_DIR/bin/conda create -n clm_gs_cpu python=3.10 -y && \
      $CONDA_DIR/bin/conda clean -afy
  # Upgrade pip and install required packages inside conda environment using conda run
  RUN conda run -n clm_gs_cpu python -m pip install --upgrade pip setuptools wheel && \
      conda run -n clm_gs_cpu pip install \
        torch==2.6.0+cpu \
        torchvision==0.21.0+cpu \
        torchaudio==2.6.0 \
        --extra-index-url https://download.pytorch.org/whl/cpu && \
      conda run -n clm_gs_cpu pip install \
        tqdm \
        plyfile \
        psutil \
        numba \
        opencv-python \
        scipy \
        matplotlib \
        pandas \
        imageio \
        imageio-ffmpeg \
        requests \
        tabulate \
        black
  WORKDIR /root
  # Clone the main repository with submodules
  RUN git clone --recursive https://github.com/nyu-systems/CLM-GS.git /root/CLM-GS
  WORKDIR /root/CLM-GS
  # Update submodules recursively (in case)
  RUN git submodule update --init --recursive
  # Install CPU-compatible submodules only, skipping clm_kernels (due to CUDA dependency)
  RUN conda run -n clm_gs_cpu pip install --no-build-isolation ./submodules/cpu-adam && \
      conda run -n clm_gs_cpu pip install ./submodules/fast-tsp && \
      conda run -n clm_gs_cpu pip install --no-build-isolation ./submodules/gsplat && \
      conda run -n clm_gs_cpu pip install --no-build-isolation ./submodules/simple-knn
  # Set default shell to bash and start at repo root with conda environment activated using conda run
  CMD ["/bin/bash", "-c", "exec /bin/bash"]

  **Step 9: Skip Offload Strategies Requiring CUDA/GPU**  
  - Do not run:  
    - Any training with `--clm_offload` (requires CUDA kernels and GPU)  
    - Any training with `--naive_offload` (CPU-GPU pinned memory transfers require GPU)  
  - Skip tests related to these strategies

  - Install and run Black as before

  ---

  - If submodule compilation fails for `clm_kernels`, skip or disable it (not needed for CPU-only training)  
  - If PyTorch CUDA-dependent imports or calls occur, ensure code paths for `--clm_offload` and `--naive_offload` are not executed  
  - Monitor CPU memory usage to prevent OOM; adjust batch size and prealloc_capacity accordingly  
  - If training is very slow on CPU, consider smaller dataset scales or hardware upgrades  
  - For dataset loading errors, confirm correct local path and dataset format  
  - Confirm no attempts to use GPU features during training or script runs

  | Aspect                          | Original Plan (GPU)                                | Adjusted Plan (CPU-only)                          |

  | GPU Driver & CUDA Toolkit       | Install CUDA 12.4 & GPU driver                    | **Omit CUDA & GPU driver installation**           |

  | Testing                       | Include CUDA availability and GPU-specific tests  | Skip CUDA/GPU tests; test CPU-only training        |

  FROM ubuntu:22.04
  ENV DEBIAN_FRONTEND=noninteractive
  ENV LANG=C.UTF-8 LC_ALL=C.UTF-8
  # Install system dependencies
  RUN apt-get update && apt-get install -y --no-install-recommends \
      git \
      curl \
      wget \
      ca-certificates \
      build-essential \
      gcc \
      g++ \
      make \
      python3.10 \

      python3-pip \

      libgl1-mesa-glx \
      libglib2.0-0 \
      bash \
      && rm -rf /var/lib/apt/lists/*
  # Symlink python3.10 to python and upgrade pip
  RUN update-alternatives --install /usr/bin/python python /usr/bin/python3.10 1 && \
      python -m pip install --upgrade pip setuptools wheel
  # Install Miniconda (latest for Linux x86_64)
  ENV CONDA_DIR=/opt/conda
  RUN wget --quiet https://repo.anaconda.com/miniconda/Miniconda3-latest-Linux-x86_64.sh -O /tmp/miniconda.sh && \
      bash /tmp/miniconda.sh -b -p $CONDA_DIR && \
      rm /tmp/miniconda.sh
  ENV PATH=$CONDA_DIR/bin:$PATH
  # Initialize conda for bash shell in Docker RUN steps
  RUN $CONDA_DIR/bin/conda init bash
  SHELL ["/bin/bash", "-c"]
  # Create conda environment clm_gs_cpu with python 3.10
  RUN conda create -n clm_gs_cpu python=3.10 -y && \
      conda clean -afy
  # Upgrade pip and install required packages inside conda environment using conda run
  RUN conda run -n clm_gs_cpu python -m pip install --upgrade pip setuptools wheel && \
      conda run -n clm_gs_cpu pip install \
        torch==2.6.0+cpu \
        torchvision==0.21.0+cpu \
        torchaudio==2.6.0 \
        --extra-index-url https://download.pytorch.org/whl/cpu && \
      conda run -n clm_gs_cpu pip install \
        tqdm \
        plyfile \
        psutil \
        numba \
        opencv-python \
        scipy \
        matplotlib \
        pandas \
        imageio \
        imageio-ffmpeg \
        requests \
        tabulate \
        black
  WORKDIR /root
  # Clone the main repository with submodules
  RUN git clone --recursive https://github.com/nyu-systems/CLM-GS.git /root/CLM-GS
  WORKDIR /root/CLM-GS
  # Update submodules recursively (in case)
  RUN git submodule update --init --recursive
  # Install CPU-compatible submodules only, skipping clm_kernels (due to CUDA dependency)
  RUN conda run -n clm_gs_cpu pip install --no-build-isolation ./submodules/cpu-adam && \
      conda run -n clm_gs_cpu pip install ./submodules/fast-tsp && \
      conda run -n clm_gs_cpu pip install --no-build-isolation ./submodules/gsplat && \
      conda run -n clm_gs_cpu pip install --no-build-isolation ./submodules/simple-knn
  # Set default shell to bash and start at repo root with conda environment activated using conda run
  CMD ["/bin/bash", "-c", "exec /bin/bash"]

  **Summary:**

The plan below is adjusted to fully support CPU-only operation, leveraging CPU training/offload modes, and ensuring compatibility with your hardware. Storage and memory requirements remain important and unchanged. This plan assumes no GPU acceleration and instructs necessary changes accordingly.

    - Minimum ~500GB free disk space recommended for MatrixCity BigCity dataset decoded images (as before)  
    - At least 50GB free disk for models/outputs  
    - Fast local disk strongly recommended especially for large datasets (avoid network filesystems)  
  - System memory:  
    - Minimum 32GB RAM recommended for regular experiments  
    - For large-scale datasets (BigCity 102M), 100GB+ CPU RAM recommended for pinned memory allocations  
    - Mip360 and Rubble 4K datasets’ CPU RAM requirements remain unchanged  
  - Optional: bash shell for running example scripts  
  - Notes on offload strategies:  
    - `--clm_offload` **can still be used** in CPU-only mode but CUDA kernels in `clm_kernels` are CUDA-based and require GPU presence; thus, **`--clm_offload` cannot be used on CPU-only systems** because it depends on CUDA and GPU drivers  
    - `--naive_offload` uses CPU pinned memory but also depends on CUDA GPU for data transfer and training; thus, **`--naive_offload` is not applicable without GPU**  
    - **Only `--no_offload` training strategy is feasible and supported on your CPU-only system** (full training on CPU without GPU offloading)  
    - `--no_offload` uses `gsplat` rendering kernels which are native CPU-compatible (compiled submodules support CPU)  
  - Version compatibility requirements:  
    - Python 3.10  
    - PyTorch 2.6.0 CPU-only build  
    - Compatible build tools (gcc/g++, make, python-dev headers) for compiling submodules  
  - Environment variables related to CUDA allocator config (`PYTORCH_CUDA_ALLOC_CONF`) are **not applicable** and should be omitted

DOCKERFILE:
  FROM ubuntu:22.04
  ENV DEBIAN_FRONTEND=noninteractive
  ENV LANG=C.UTF-8 LC_ALL=C.UTF-8
  # Install system dependencies
  RUN apt-get update && apt-get install -y --no-install-recommends \
      git \
      curl \
      wget \
      ca-certificates \
      build-essential \
      gcc \
      g++ \
      make \
      python3.10 \
      python3.10-dev \
      python3-pip \
      python3-setuptools \
      python3-venv \
      libgl1-mesa-glx \
      libglib2.0-0 \
      bash \
      && rm -rf /var/lib/apt/lists/*
  # Symlink python3.10 to python and upgrade pip
  RUN update-alternatives --install /usr/bin/python python /usr/bin/python3.10 1 && \
      python -m pip install --upgrade pip setuptools wheel
  # Install Miniconda (latest for Linux x86_64)
  ENV CONDA_DIR=/opt/conda
  RUN wget --quiet https://repo.anaconda.com/miniconda/Miniconda3-latest-Linux-x86_64.sh -O /tmp/miniconda.sh && \
      bash /tmp/miniconda.sh -b -p $CONDA_DIR && \
      rm /tmp/miniconda.sh
  ENV PATH=$CONDA_DIR/bin:$PATH
  # Initialize conda for bash shell in Docker RUN steps
  RUN $CONDA_DIR/bin/conda init bash
  SHELL ["/bin/bash", "-c"]
  # Create conda environment clm_gs_cpu with python 3.10 using sourced conda.sh
  RUN source $CONDA_DIR/etc/profile.d/conda.sh && \
      conda create -n clm_gs_cpu python=3.10 -y && \
      conda clean -afy
  # Upgrade pip and install required packages inside conda environment using conda run
  RUN source $CONDA_DIR/etc/profile.d/conda.sh && \
      conda run -n clm_gs_cpu python -m pip install --upgrade pip setuptools wheel && \
      conda run -n clm_gs_cpu pip install \
        torch==2.6.0+cpu \
        torchvision==0.21.0+cpu \
        torchaudio==2.6.0 \
        --extra-index-url https://download.pytorch.org/whl/cpu && \
      conda run -n clm_gs_cpu pip install \
        tqdm \
        plyfile \
        psutil \
        numba \
        opencv-python \
        scipy \
        matplotlib \
        pandas \
        imageio \
        imageio-ffmpeg \
        requests \
        tabulate \
        black
  WORKDIR /root
  # Clone the main repository with submodules
  RUN git clone --recursive https://github.com/nyu-systems/CLM-GS.git /root/CLM-GS
  WORKDIR /root/CLM-GS
  # Update submodules recursively (in case)
  RUN git submodule update --init --recursive
  # Install CPU-compatible submodules only, skipping clm_kernels (due to CUDA dependency)
  RUN source $CONDA_DIR/etc/profile.d/conda.sh && \
      conda run -n clm_gs_cpu pip install --no-build-isolation ./submodules/cpu-adam && \
      conda run -n clm_gs_cpu pip install ./submodules/fast-tsp && \
      conda run -n clm_gs_cpu pip install --no-build-isolation ./submodules/gsplat && \
      conda run -n clm_gs_cpu pip install --no-build-isolation ./submodules/simple-knn
  # Set default shell to bash and start at repo root with conda environment activated using conda run
  CMD ["/bin/bash", "-c", "source /opt/conda/etc/profile.d/conda.sh && conda activate clm_gs_cpu && exec /bin/bash"]
